Huashang Company Received Telegram from Qingdao Yesterday: Haihua Ship Lost, Crew Safe

According to Qingdao telegraphic news obtained by shipping circles yesterday, it was learned that the Haihua ship had an accident in Qingdao. Special notes are made as follows: Haihua ship of Huashang Shipping Company, located at 160 Aiduwu Road, has always sailed in the North and South Seas, mainly loading goods and not carrying passengers. Because the ship needed to load Xinhua coal to Shanghai, it set sail for Qingdao empty on the 23rd of this month. The voyage out of the Shanghai port was relatively smooth.

Encountered Wind Arriving at Port

At around 7:00 AM yesterday morning, the ship had already sailed into Qingdao Port, near the port-facing misty area of ​​the radio station. Continued with a strong wind, ship captain Zhang Meibin was seeking for safe passage and approached the harbor slowly, but the area near the vicinity inside the harbor has submerged reefs. The Haihua ship, under the pressure of the storm, suddenly hit a reef and immediately created a gaping hole. Water rushed into the cabin, and the ship soon began to sink. The situation was very critical.

Crew Escaped

The ship was empty, and there were no passengers or cargo in the cabins. Once the vessel hit the reef and water started flooding in, Captain Zhang Meibin urgently sought to control the damage, but was unable to do anything. He ordered all the crew, stokers, and other personnel to quickly leave the ship and go ashore to avoid accidents. He immediately asked the Qingdao agent, Xing Ji Company, to quickly send a telegram to the Shanghai head office to report and instruct how to proceed. It was not until yesterday afternoon that the Shanghai office received the alarm.

Notifying All Parties

The Haihua ship has an marine insurance policy of 80,000 yuan. Huashang Shipping Company relayed the original telegram to the China Ship Insurance Federation, stating that "The Haihua ship departed from Shanghai for Qingdao on the 23rd of this month to load coal. Unexpectedly, we just received a telegram from the agent Xing Ji, stating that the Haihua ship entered the port at 7:30 this morning (the 25th). It encountered a hurricane and fog and was flooded inside the cabin near the radio station. The crew landed safely. Please notify accordingly. etc."

Ship Status

The Haihua ship was built in 1920, originally named Spolanne. It was purchased by a Chinese merchant and renamed to its current name. The hull is made of steel, with a deadweight of 2,103 tons, a net tonnage of 1,216 tons, and can load 3,350 tons of cargo. The ship is 251 feet 6 inches long, 43 feet 5 inches wide, 23 feet 1 inch deep, has a draft of 20 feet, and a speed of 9.5 to 10 nautical miles per hour. It burns 20 to 21 tons of coal per hour, has one deck, 4 bulkheads, and a Triple engine with a horsepower of 216. The ship was built by Toronto's Dominion S. B. & Reporing factory in Norway.

County Districts Report on Crop Failure Due to Disasters

The cotton and rice crops planted in the agricultural lands of Shanghai County's districts have suffered damage from wind and rain, as well as insect infestations, resulting in crop failure. The County Assets Office and other departments had previously submitted reports to the provincial authorities. Now, according to reports submitted by all district chiefs of the county to the county government, this year's autumn harvest is generally no more than 60% of normal. They requested relief to alleviate the people's hardship. County Magistrate Ye, after reviewing the reports, submitted the county's disaster situation to the Jiangsu Provincial Government and the Civil Affairs and Finance Departments for review and instructions on how to proceed.

China International Famine Relief Commission Launches Xie Andao Memorial Fund

Mr. Xie Andao, born in California, USA, was dispatched to the Chinese National Council of YMCAs by the YMCA of New York in 1905 to report on its work. He has been working in China for nearly 30 years. He founded the YMCAs in Chengdu and Chongqing. In the past two years, he served as the chief secretary of the Shanghai office of the China International Famine Relief Commission. Unfortunately, he fell ill in July of this year and passed away on September 29 despite medical treatment. His will stipulated that funeral arrangements should be simple and that any condolence money from relatives and friends should be used for disaster relief and donated to the China International Famine Relief Commission for collection. The National Association of Chinese Christian Youth Associations, recognizing Xie's long service and significant contributions to the association, allocated 5,000 yuan to the China International Famine Relief Commission for disaster relief in accordance with his will to fulfill his wishes. His relatives and friends also donated condolence money, totaling over 300 yuan, which the commission has received. Therefore, the commission, in memory of Xie, launched the Xie Andao Memorial Fund. The executive committee of the China International Famine Relief Commission resolved that the memorial fund would be used for loans to provide relief for water and drought disasters, as well as to improve agricultural industries, but the principal of the fund should not be used. The fund will be entrusted to the Yangtze River Basin Rehabilitation Commission for safekeeping. Xie's concern for disaster victims in our country and the fulfillment of Xie's lifelong aspiration by his relatives and friends are commendable. Given Xie's wide circle of friends, there will surely be continuing contributions to comfort Xie's spirit and save the lives of disaster victims, truly achieving both aims at once.

Water Disaster Relief Association Commemorates Zhang Zepu

The Shanghai Association for Raising Funds for Water Disaster Relief in Various Provinces received a report from Li Du, the magistrate of Yude County, Anhui, regarding Zhang Zepu, the former deputy director of drought investigation and relief, requesting a commendation. The report states, "According to the report from Lin Jinwen, permanent committee member of the disaster relief committee of our county, Dong Yutian, chairman of the finance committee, Jin Zhaonan, chairman of the chamber of commerce, Zhu Xuecheng, staff member of the farmers' association, Ji Fatang, staff member of the education association, etc., Mr. Zhang Zepu, the deputy director of the Anhui Investigation and Relief Office of the Shanghai Association for Raising Funds for Drought Disaster Relief in Various Provinces, has been handling relief matters for thirty years. During the recent major disasters in our province, he personally went to provide relief, conducting thorough investigations and providing assistance, saving countless lives. His actions have been repeatedly praised by superiors, and the facts are well documented and need no further elaboration. Last year, our county suffered from both drought and bandits, and the local economy was severely damaged. This summer, we suffered from flood disaster again, and most of the county became a flooded area. Fields and crops were submerged, and houses were washed away. Dozens of villages were without smoke from cooking fires, and hundreds of households had no grain. Director Zhang, together with Director Wang Ganshi and other staff members, came to our county last winter under orders, bringing funds to provide relief for pregnant women affected by the drought. He personally went to the disaster areas to conduct on-site investigations and provide assistance. Our disaster victims were suddenly showered with the water of compassion, and the parched lands were revived. Recalling the great kindness of the assistance, we are deeply grateful. Moreover, Zhang Gong also saw that there was not enough food for everyone and that it was difficult to continue. He taught us to thoroughly provide disaster relief, leaving no effort unspent. He then founded a porridge kitchen without using fire, personally traveling to Tianjin, Beijing, and Shanghai to appeal for help, raising huge sums of money over a period of ten days. He did not mind the hardship of traveling, and he personally took out money from his own pocket for travel expenses. If he were not generous and righteous, how could he be so enthusiastic? It goes without saying that the distribution of relief to the disaster areas and the investigation and assistance were thorough. Moreover, the staff members he brought were able to risk traveling through dangerous bandit areas, cooperating with local people to conduct on-site investigations. Therefore, all the refugees in the disaster areas received real benefits and praised his efforts. This summer, the flood victims in our county suffered even more than during the major flood of 1931. Director Zhang saw the severity of the disaster and the cries of the refugees. He discussed with you and tried his best to raise money and borrow food, as well as various medicines, and ventured into the raging waves, providing food and comfort to the awaiting people. He braved the sun and the heat, and the sweat soaked his back. He did not avoid any hardship and provided ten days of emergency relief, bringing the people to safety. This is what is meant by saving people from a well, not caring about anything else. Unexpectedly, while traveling on a boat with a red head, he was injured in his right arm while circumventing the water around the mountains. The pain was deep, but he avoided seeking medical treatment and continued to inspect the disaster area despite his illness. We were planning to submit a request for praise to highlight his merits, but heaven was unforgiving. Zhang Gong suddenly passed away in Beijing at the end of August due to a serious illness. When the bad news arrived, all the disaster victims in the county mourned deeply. In addition to sending a special telegram of condolences and a telegram to the Central Relief Committee to request the National Government to provide generous compensation, we respectfully submit the facts of Zhang Gong's relief efforts, to the best of our knowledge, and briefly describe his good deeds throughout his life. We are deeply grateful for his righteousness and are saddened by his poverty after his death. How will his family survive? We jointly present this document, requesting your approval and submission to the Anhui Provincial Government to grant generous compensation to comfort his spirit and ensure the well-being of his surviving family members. Based on this, after reviewing the statements made by the committee members, it is found that all the facts are accurate. We respectfully submit this document, and in addition to submitting it to the Anhui Provincial Government, we respectfully request your review and approval to grant generous compensation to comfort his spirit and ensure the well-being of his surviving family members, which would be a virtuous act." This matter was raised at the fourth joint meeting of the standing directors and supervisors of the association yesterday. It was reported that the official had been handling relief efforts for many years and had worked diligently and made outstanding achievements. He sacrificed his life for relief work, which is deeply regrettable and mourned. After joint discussion, it was decided that in addition to the Central Relief Committee providing generous compensation in accordance with regulations, the Drought Disaster Relief Association would provide a one-time compensation of 500 yuan, and the Flood Disaster Relief Association would provide a one-time compensation of 300 yuan to encourage and show compassion. Mr. Zhang Xiaolin, director of the review committee of the association, who happened to be present at the meeting that day, generously donated 200 national currency yuan to support Zhang's orphaned children. Such kindness and righteousness are not only appreciated by Zhang, both living and dead, but also admired by all people. Such excellent compassion for those who have worked hard and diligently in disaster relief is enough to encourage others.

Relief Efforts of the China International Famine Relief Commission

The China International Famine Relief Commission on Renji Road believes that the water disaster is most severe in northern Jiangsu. Following the major drought, it established a branch in Peixian, Xuzhou, and successively allocated 12,000 yuan in relief funds and medicines for emergency relief. However, the Yellow River overflowed to the south, and although the current situation has gradually stabilized, the disaster area has expanded, the number of refugees has increased, and the tragic situation is rare. Moreover, autumn is already deep and the weather is cold, so relief is urgently needed. An additional relief office was established in Yaowan, Pizhou, to supplement the areas that are not being assisted. The areas of Haizhou have also suffered greatly. Because of the difficulty in providing comprehensive assistance, the commission is working with the Jisheng Society and is allocating funds to transport clothing. The emergency relief to various disaster-stricken counties in Shandong was previously overseen by Director Lu Bohong. A branch has since been established in Jining, and a total of 50,000 yuan in relief funds has been allocated to the various counties as follows: Dongping 10,000 yuan, Juancheng 10,000 yuan, Yutai 13,000 yuan, Yuncheng and Shouzhang 5,000 yuan each, Juye and Heze 2,500 yuan each, and Jinxiang 2,000 yuan. It is also reported that the commission believes that while emergency relief is crucial for saving lives, the water disaster has left many people without a thread of clothing, so clothing is especially necessary. The commission has first produced 15,000 sets of cotton clothing, which will be shipped to Jiangsu and Shandong as soon as the procedures for free transportation are completed to meet the urgent need. As for the Yangtze River relief efforts, in addition to the initial emergency relief to the Tianmen disaster area, 7,000 yuan has been allocated and jointly distributed with the Jisheng Society. However, the area is too large, so another 20,000 yuan has been allocated and is being carried out in conjunction with the Red Swastika Society. Over sixty boxes of clothing sent by overseas Chinese and local organizations in Shanghai have also been transported for distribution. Secondly, 20,000 yuan has been allocated to the disaster area in Hunan, and Director Lu Bohong is responsible for supervising the distribution by the local branch. Furthermore, 5,000 yuan has been allocated to Fujian Province and handed over to the Quanzhou Chinese and Western Committee for handling. In Guangdong Province, 5,000 yuan will be allocated to Sihui and Guangning for targeted relief. The commission has recently received over 12,000 yuan from overseas Chinese in the United States, over 14,000 yuan from various places in Nanyang, 24 boxes of old clothes, 16 boxes of old clothes from the Philippines, 38 bags, over 10,000 yuan from various great philanthropists, 1,000 bottles of Supreme Oil from the Supreme Company, and 1,000 bottles of Shidi Shui (Ten Drops Water) from Mr. Yang Jifang.

Exemption from Taxes for Land Requisitioned for River Dredging in County Districts

The land survey in various districts of Shanghai County has been completed. However, as the agricultural slack season approaches, each district must requisition labor to dredge rivers. The farmland along the rivers will inevitably have to be requisitioned, which will affect the payment of taxes on the already surveyed land. Therefore, after discussion at yesterday's land consolidation meeting, it was decided that when land along rivers is requisitioned for dredging, the land bureau should survey and revise the maps, and a request should be submitted to the county government to exempt the requisitioned land from taxes.

China National Aviation Corporation's special express flight between Shanghai and Chengdu, which arrives on the same day, was previously announced to fly to Chengdu on Tuesdays and Fridays and return to Shanghai on Wednesdays and Saturdays. It is now scheduled to change from Monday, October 28th, to fly from Shanghai to Chengdu on Mondays and Thursdays and return from Chengdu to Shanghai on Tuesdays and Fridays, with both round trips arriving on the same day.

Emerging National Waterproofing Products for Cement Buildings

In recent years, China's construction industry has been developing rapidly. Regarding design issues, such as high-rise buildings, not only have they become magnificent and spectacular, but the dryness and brightness of the interior are also of great importance to health and hygiene, as well as to all properties. If the walls and floors are invaded by dampness, wind, and rain, causing them to be unable to dry quickly, all properties and health will suffer greatly. Various countries have long been studying waterproofing projects in order to preserve the safety of the interior. The Jianye Trading Company has hired chemical experts to invent Jianye Waterproofing Powder. After the Pudong Fellow Villagers Association and Caojia Garden in Caohejing have used it for building waterproofing projects, it has proven to be greatly effective and has achieved great success. It is now sold throughout the country and is praised by all sectors. For building construction projects such as houses, cellars, pools, water towers, bridge piles, dams, and swimming pools, using Jianye Waterproofing Powder can guarantee special effects, far superior to imported products and much better than oil felt. When purchasing, stating that you were referred by the Chinese Institute of Engineers can get considerable discounts.

Shanghai Public Security Bureau Proclamation: Strict Prohibition of Jinji Lingbao Pills

The Shanghai Public Security Bureau issued Proclamation No. 170 yesterday, stating: "It is hereby announced that within the Instruction No. 4016 (Law) of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, it is stated, 'Upon investigation of the Wang Li and others drug case, Jinji Lingbao pills were seized. These pills have been sent to the Forensic Medicine Research Institute and the Hygiene Testing Laboratory for chemical testing, and opium and other reactions have been found. They should be strictly investigated and prohibited. It is also reported that various pills sold on the market, such as Ningshi pills, contain toxic substances. Samples should be purchased separately and sent to the laboratory for chemical testing. If opium, morphine, or other ingredients are found, their sale should be strictly prohibited, and a proclamation should be issued to inform the public and clear the atmosphere of poison. The above is an order to the Director of the Bureau to immediately comply and report accordingly. Therefore, in compliance with the above, the Investigation Section of the Inspection Office of the Bureau sent personnel to search for Jinji Lingbao pills and Ningbao pills in the tobacco and paper shops in the French Concession and seized one package of each, which was about to be sent to the Hygiene Testing Laboratory for chemical testing. Following that, Instruction No. 4261 (Law) of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters was received, stating, 'The case of Liu Bingxin carrying Ningbao pills, which was submitted by the Bureau, has been adjudicated by this Headquarters according to law. Upon investigation, these Ningbao pills were sent to the Municipal Hygiene Testing Laboratory for chemical testing, and reactions of morphine and opium acid were found. Moreover, the sale of these pills was previously strictly prohibited by the Headquarters in Order No. 416 (Law) of June of this year. The Director of the Bureau is ordered to comply and instruct subordinates to strictly prohibit the sale of these pills in order to clear the atmosphere of poison.' Therefore, in addition to instructing subordinates to strictly investigate and prohibit the sale of these pills, a proclamation is hereby issued to inform the public."

Go Gongzhen's Burial Site Determined: In the First Municipal Cemetery, to be Requested from the Municipal Government

The famous journalist Go Gongzhen passed away a few days ago and was placed in a coffin the day before yesterday. With the consent of Go's family, obtained by the funeral committee, it was decided that Go's remains would be publicly buried in the Shanghai Municipal Cemetery. Yesterday afternoon at 2 PM, Go's elder brother Shudong, cousin Xianglan, and Mr. Huang Jiping visited Director Pan of the Education Bureau to discuss the matter of the burial site. Pan sent a representative, Zhou Yongxing, to accompany them to survey the First Municipal Cemetery on Sanmin Road in the central district. Under the guidance of Gong Zishan, the administrator of the cemetery, a site was tentatively selected. The site consists of four grave plots, allowing for the erection of a tombstone and the establishment of a bronze statue. The funeral committee will draft a memorial and submit it to the Municipal Government for allocation. Approval is expected. Shanghai Branch of the National Bank of Hong Kong Opens Debt Registration Yesterday, but Bondholders Oppose Liquidation

National News Agency, Shanghai, October 25th. The liquidation office of the Shanghai branch of the National Bank of Hong Kong began registering debts today. Many people went to register, accounting for half of the total debt amount. The office printed letters inquiring whether creditors agreed to the bank's re-establishment after liquidation. Almost all of those who signed agreed. All of the creditors in Hong Kong agreed to the re-establishment. Yesterday, the office received a telegram from the representative of the Hong Kong creditors, stating that a second meeting of all the bank's creditors would be convened within three weeks to discuss the re-establishment. It is also reported that the liquidation office will also convene a meeting of the Shanghai branch's creditors within two or three weeks to discuss the issue.

Xin Xin News Agency reports: The bondholders of the Shanghai branch of the National Bank of Hong Kong have specially hired lawyer Liang Yaobing to announce their opposition to the liquidation and petition the court to declare the bank bankrupt. The announcement is as follows: "According to the above-mentioned creditors, after reading various newspaper advertisements and seeing three news items about the liquidation of the Shanghai branch of the National Bank of Hong Kong, they were extremely surprised. It was found that Chu Zhongqing was originally the general manager of the bank's various branches, and the other liquidators were absolutely interested parties of the bank. The liquidation by them is not in accordance with human sentiments and the law and is prone to abuses. The creditors are afraid that their claims will be infringed upon and, in order to protect their legal interests, they will petition the court to declare the bank bankrupt and request the appointment of a bankruptcy administrator. The court is currently awaiting a decision. Please publish an objection. All creditors should listen to the court's decision to avoid losing their claims."

Death of Mr. Pan Xulun's Mother

The mother of Mr. Pan Xulun, director of the Lixin Accountants' Office in this city, passed away at the age of eighty. She recently contracted a minor illness in her hometown of Yixing. Both Chinese and Western doctors were consulted, but due to her advanced age, she passed away on the 22nd of this month. Page 11

Nine-Year-Old Grandson, Shan Cheng, Kidnapped, Held in Bandit's Lair for Over Eighty Days, Safe Return Reveals Lively Child Without Abnormalities, Kidnappers Demand Exorbitant Ransom of 500,000 Yuan, Male and Female Kidnappers Interrogated and Awaiting Scheduled Sentencing

Sun Cailing, a 40-year-old native of Dinghai, Zhejiang, residing at No. 344, Lane 3, Beile Road in the French Concession, and working in the banking industry, had a beloved nine-year-old son named Shan Cheng. On the afternoon of August 5th of this year, Shan Cheng went to play at the home of Sun's younger brother, Sun Caizhang, nearby and suddenly disappeared. At the same time, the maid of the Zhang household, Yu Tang, also known as Cai Xian or Genhua, from Shaoxing, was also missing. As the family was in a state of panic, Sun found a letter in his home that had been slipped in from the outside. The letter stated that his son had been kidnapped and demanded an overseas ransom of 500,000 yuan, instructing him to contact them at a certain location for negotiations. Only then did they realize that the child had been abducted by kidnappers. They immediately reported it to the police, requesting investigation and arrest. The Chinese and Western detectives of the French Concession police department went out in all directions to gather clues and apprehend the kidnappers. It was not until September 12th that they arrested the kidnappers' accomplices, Ying Caifang (44 years old) from Shaoxing, Wang Wenhua (also known as Fenghuang's eldest son, 35 years old), Chen Genlin (45 years old), a woman named Chen Tang (also known as Tu Xian, 32 years old, and sister of the maid Yu Tang who disappeared at the same time as the hostage), Zhang Xiaofu (40 years old, a carpenter residing at No. 218 Wangzhi Road), and five other men and women. They then proceeded to Hangzhou to arrest Wang Baoshan (56 years old) from Shaoxing and brought him to Shanghai to be jointly escorted to the Second Special District Court.

The investigation and detention were carried out according to regulations. The whereabouts of the hostage were unknown at the time of the investigation, so the matter was kept secret and not disclosed. Later, the arrested suspect Ying Caifang died of illness while in custody. Although the Second Special Court held several hearings, led by Judge Zhang Chaozuo, the defendants all shirked responsibility and denied involvement in the kidnapping. As a result, it was difficult to obtain any clues about the whereabouts of the hostage. The French Concession police continued to investigate rigorously, but still found no leads. The case was originally scheduled for a retrial by the court. Yesterday, appointed lawyer Bian Kuang was summoned to court for further questioning. On the morning of the day before yesterday (the 24th), at 7:30 AM, the plaintiff suddenly

received a phone call stating that the child Sun Shancheng was in Room 32 of the China Hotel on Jiujiang Road in the Public Concession, requesting that he be taken back immediately. The plaintiff immediately reported the information to the French Concession police, who dispatched detectives along with the Chinese and Western detectives from the Old Gate police station to assist in rushing to Room 32 of the China Hotel at No. 456 Jiujiang Road. They found the hostage, the child Sun Shancheng, alone in the room, with no one else inside. They inquired with the hotel's accountant and staff, who stated that a person claiming to be Chen Bin had checked into Room 32 on the night of the 23rd,

stayed overnight, and then extended the room for another night, taking the child away at night. However, Sun Shancheng, who had been held in the kidnappers' lair for over eighty days, was still lively and showed no signs of abnormality. He was immediately taken back to the French Concession police station for questioning and then handed over to his family to take back. Yesterday at noon, Judge Zhang of the Second Special Court visited the First Criminal Court to interrogate the defendants who had been arrested earlier. The lawyer representing the police department, Gu Shouxi, stated to the court that the hostage in the case had been found yesterday in the China Hotel and was now

safe and sound. The investigating detective then reported the circumstances of the rescue of the hostage. The plaintiff, Sun Cailing, also brought his son Shancheng to court, stating that the child disappeared between 2:00 and 3:00 PM on August 5th. Later, he found a letter left behind by the kidnappers in his home and received three more letters. When the court questioned the kidnapped child Sun Shancheng, he testified, "That day, the nanny with a scar on her neck took me out to a Chinese-style house. There was a girl named Lin Zhen who played with me. When I made noise, I was beaten." When asked if he recognized any of the defendants in court, Shancheng

looked around at the faces of the defendants and shook his head, indicating that he did not recognize them. According to the detective's report, the hostage was taken to the police station and questioned. He stated that the nanny took him out of the lane to a crossroads and handed him over to a man who took him away in a rickshaw. He was transferred to three different locations, but never left Shanghai. When the court questioned the defendant Chen Tang, she stated, "Yu Tang is my younger sister, and the girl Lin Zhen is my niece. I raised her. I really don't know anything about the kidnapping." The other defendants also denied any involvement in the kidnapping. At this point, the court considered the facts of the case to be clear and ordered the commencement of arguments. After the police department's lawyer presented his arguments, the appointed lawyers Jin Xinmin, Gao Danhua, and others defended the defendants. The court then declared the arguments closed and scheduled sentencing for the morning of the 31st. The defendants were returned to custody.

The public notice is appended below: Public Notice from the Land Bureau: In order to facilitate certificate change, the current location of the City Land Bureau in the city center will be switched to that of the Public Works Bureau in accordance with the City Government instructions. It has been decided in consultation with the Public Works Bureau that the relocation will begin on November 1st of this year. From November 4th onwards, the office will be located at the original site of the Public Works Bureau (east of the Financial Bureau on Fenglin Road), and business will continue as usual. This concerns the relocation of the office, and this public notice is hereby issued to inform the people of the city.

Creditors of Taifeng Company Pass Settlement Plan, Deadline for Resumption of Business

Regarding the case of the Nanjing Road Taifeng Canned Food Co., Ltd. declaring liquidation, the First Special District Court of this city originally ruled to allow the debtor to declare liquidation on April 22. Subsequently, the court approved the application of creditors such as the Tongqing Money Shop to apply the bankruptcy reconciliation procedure in accordance with Article 1 of the Bankruptcy Implementation Law and Chapter 2, Section 1 of the Bankruptcy Law. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, a creditors' meeting was convened at the Hubei Club on Guizhou Road to discuss the proposed revised settlement plan. After voting, it was passed. After the court approves the settlement, the company will open for business within two and a half months. The details are as follows as reported by the reporters of the Da Gong She:

Creditors' Meeting

After the First Special District Court approved the creditors' application and announced the liquidation of Taifeng Company, the court convened a creditors' meeting at the Hubei Club yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM in accordance with bankruptcy law and the reconciliation procedure. Judge Yu Lude, designated supervisor of the court, appointed Li Ding, an accountant, and Qiu Fenling, a lawyer, as assistant supervisors. Creditor representatives Xu Zuyan, representing the money industry, Zhu Fuju, representing depositors, and Xiang Kangyuan, representing goods suppliers, with a right to vote of 473,000, and debtor representatives Qin Liankui and Xu Yongzuo, the original liquidator and accountant, attended. Yu Lude chaired the meeting. After announcing the opening of the meeting, Xu Yongzuo, the liquidator, first reported the accounts (omitted). The chairman then presented the settlement plan for discussion. Subsequently, Xu Zuyan, a lawyer representing the money industry creditors, and Zhu Fuju, a lawyer representing the depositor creditors (representing more than 300,000 in debt), jointly proposed revising the original settlement plan. After the chairman put it to a vote, 194 votes were in favor and one vote was against, passing the revised plan. According to the total debt of 567,000, with 427,077.33 yuan of debt in favor and 190 yuan against, the standard for adjudication is that the debt must exceed 425,441.43 yuan. The supervisors will submit it to the court for adjudication and implementation. Representatives were elected to supervise the implementation of the settlement plan after the court's adjudication. The money industry representatives were Xu Zuyan and Sun Hou, the depositor representatives were Zhu Fuju and Fei Wenbao, and the goods creditor representative was Xiang Kangyuan. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM.

Settlement Plan

The original text of the revised settlement plan is recorded as follows: (1) Taifeng Company's external debts are estimated at 550,000 yuan in principal and interest. 10% will be paid first, estimated at 55,000 yuan, in cash by the liquidator on the day following the adjudication of the settlement. (2) For the remaining 90% of Taifeng Company's external debts, half of the amount will be paid by the board of directors at a rate of 20% per year after the company resumes business, to be paid off in five years. Before the debt is paid off, creditors will send representatives to supervise the finances. (3) For the remaining half of the 90% of Taifeng Company's external debts in addition to the first and second items, the company bonds will bear an annual interest of 6%, starting from the sixth year, and one-fifth of the principal will be repaid each year. However, when the company's business develops, the company should repay and recover the bonds early. (4) All of Taifeng Company's external old claims, and the claims against the Huaming Match Factory, as well as the movable and immovable property of the Huaming Factory, will be used as security for the second item of this settlement plan. When this claim is recovered, or the movable and immovable property is converted into cash, regardless of the amount, it should be used to repay the debt mentioned in the second item as soon as possible. If the Huaming claim is fully recovered, and the debt in the second item has been paid off, and there is still a surplus, it will be used to repay part of the company bonds in advance. (5) All matters related to the collection, conversion, and distribution of Taifeng Company's external claims, and the claims against the Huaming Factory, as well as the movable and immovable property of the Huaming Factory, will still be handled jointly by the original liquidator, Li Ding, an accountant, Qiu Fenling, a lawyer, and the lawyer representatives appointed by the creditors. Taifeng Company may not freely settle or abandon any claims without the consent of the above three persons. (6) All of Taifeng Company's movable and immovable property will be used as collateral and security for the company bonds mentioned in the third item of this settlement plan. The company may not re-mortgage or pledge these collateral and security items externally. (7) Creditors may elect representatives to keep the collateral and security items mentioned in the sixth item. (8) The company bonds mentioned in the third item should be submitted to the company. If the company does not open for business within two and a half months after the establishment of this settlement plan, the settlement plan will be canceled.

Japanese Take Strict Precautions for Shanghai Shrine Autumn Festival

According to the Japanese Daily News, November 1st, 2nd and 3rd are the dates for the Japanese residents to worship at the Shanghai Shrine. On the 23rd, the Japanese Club, the Japanese Consulate General, the Marine Corps, the Public Works Bureau, and other related parties held a security committee meeting to determine the security policy as follows: (1) For three days, from 10:00 AM to afternoon, the passage of vehicles will be prohibited on the road from the Marine Corps Headquarters to Hongkou Park. (2) The terminus of public buses will be changed to in front of Zhien Temple. (3) Carrying animals into the venue is prohibited. (4) For easy identification, entrants must wear Western or Japanese clothing. (5) News reporters and photographers must obtain armbands from the Civil Defense Corps. (6) Everyone's belongings must be subject to inspection at any time. (7) Cars entering the venue must be parked in front of the Hongkou Park gate.

Feili Automobile Company Discovers Suspicious Accounts, Several Dubious Gift Accounts, Shareholder Chen Ronghai Files Lawsuit

Liu Guojin, a native of Yangzhou, raised funds to establish the Feili Automobile Company on Xiaoshadu Road in western Shanghai in the 20th year of the Republic of China. He served as the general manager himself, and his clansmen Liu Defa and Liu Guojing served as manager and accountant, respectively. Since the company began operations, it has been almost five years, and it has never prepared financial statements for distribution to shareholders. As a result, some shareholders have been quite dissatisfied. Chen Ronghai, also a shareholder, recently negotiated with Liu et al. through his grandfather, requesting an investigation of the company's accounts over the years, but Liu refused. Chen then filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Court. When Liu appeared in court, he expressed his willingness to submit the accounts for review. Once he left the court, however, he refused to comply. The court then ordered Liu to be detained, and sent bailiffs along with the plaintiff to the company to briefly examine the account books. They discovered several accounts under the name of gifts, (1) 100 yuan to the Yao family between those who processed license renewals. (2) 50 yuan to the Wu family during the license renewals. (3) 50 yuan for sampling. (4) 108 yuan for the police station's winter solstice gifts. (5) 50 yuan to Cokes. (6) 100 yuan for telephone installation. Chen and his grandson believed that the above accounts were suspicious and were fabricated by Liu et al. to embezzle the funds. They hired lawyer Huang Xiubo to file a criminal private prosecution against Liu Guojin for embezzlement and breach of trust. A hearing has already been held once, and the case has been adjourned to the afternoon of yesterday to continue the hearing, as it is necessary to summon more witnesses. The plaintiff also filed lawsuits against Liu Defa and Liu Guojing for embezzlement and breach of trust. The defendants denied any

collusion or fraud and filed a counterclaim against Chen, accusing him of fabricating facts and requesting that he be punished for false accusation. The presiding judge Liu Yugui first questioned the witnesses Shi Guilan and Gao about whether the gift amounts in the accounts were real. The witnesses stated that Liu Guojin had reported to the shareholders afterwards. The court then questioned Liu about the names of the Yao and Wu families and who received the telephone installation fee, but he claimed that he did not know their names. After the lawyers for both parties argued, Judge Liu

scheduled the sentencing for the morning of October 29.

Argument Over Three Yuan in Rent Leads to Incident, Woman Dies from Injuries, Forensic Doctor Believes Cause of Death Cannot Be Ascertained Without Autopsy

Zhu Xu, a 58-year-old local woman, lived at No. 4, Lane 357, Tianjin Road. She had rented a spare room to Shi Chen, a woman from Huzhou. Shi owed three yuan in rent, and Zhu went to collect it the afternoon before last at 5:00 PM, leading to an argument. Shi Chen pushed Zhu Xu violently, and Zhu fell to the ground, immediately losing consciousness. She was sent to the hospital for treatment, but the treatment was ineffective, and she died at 11:15 PM. The Old Gate police station was notified and ordered Chinese detective Feng Xiushan to arrest Shi Chen. She was sent to the First Criminal Court of the First Special District Court yesterday morning. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang charged her under Article 278, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Code. Since an examination was still needed, he requested that the case be adjourned. Judge Qian Hongye approved the request. Subsequently, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court visited the body to examine it. According to the forensic doctor's report, the cause of Zhu Xu's death could not be ascertained without an autopsy. Therefore, he instructed that the case be heard again after the autopsy.

Yuan Dagui Goes Insane, Cuts Daughter-in-Law with Knife

Yuan Dagui, a 57-year-old native of Ningbo, lives at No. 7, Lane 144, Tangen Road. His son works on a ship and is often away from home. His daughter-in-law, Wang, lives alone downstairs, while Yuan sleeps in a loft. He has recently suffered from insanity, which comes and goes. He often speaks inappropriately to Wang. At 7:40 AM the day before yesterday, Wang was still asleep, and Yuan suddenly climbed in through the window with a firewood knife, cutting Wang on the head without asking why. She bled profusely and cried out for help. Yuan abandoned the knife and fled. Chinese detectives Zhang Degong and Qi Fanglian from the Jiaxing Road police station arrived after hearing the alarm and arrested him, bringing him and the firewood knife back to the police station. The injured party was taken to the nursing home for treatment. Yuan Dagui was sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court yesterday. Public Works Bureau lawyer Zhang Shizhu stated the previous situation, and said that the defendant had been entering his daughter-in-law's bedroom to harass her in the mornings. It is not known whether he is insane. The victim is in the hospital and cannot testify in court, so he requests a postponement. The detectives then reported the arrest, presenting the firewood knife for inspection. When questioned, Yuan Dagui stated that the firewood knife belonged to him. When asked why he cut his daughter-in-law, he remained silent. A young woman named Li Wang stated that the injured party was her younger sister and Yuan Dagui's daughter-in-law. When he has an episode, he is abusive or violent. Judge Xiao Fen instructed that the case must be adjourned, the defendant returned to custody, and a doctor should examine him.

Empty Sampan Full of Bloodstains: Chen Jichang's Whereabouts Unknown, Likely Murdered; Parents Weep and Report to Police After Hearing of Impending Marriage and Death

Chen Lansheng, a native of Ningbo, residing at No. 45 Renji Lane, Renji Road, Pudong, used to row a sampan. Now, due to his advanced age, hearing loss, and failing eyesight, he handed over his own sampan, No. 50, to his son, Jichang, to operate. Jichang, currently 21 years old, continues his father's profession, ferrying passengers at the Chunjiang Wharf in Pudong. Around 8 PM the night before last, during a heavy downpour, three men dressed in short attire hailed Jichang's sampan, stating they wanted to cross to the Mitsubishi Company Wharf in Hongkou. Jichang quoted a fare of four dimes. One of them, speaking with a Ningbo accent, haggled down to three dimes, claiming they were also people from the boats and should give them a break. This was known by all the sampans in the area. After Jichang rowed the sampan away, his whereabouts became unknown. He did not return until daybreak. Yesterday morning at 10:05 AM, Chinese Constable No. 24 of the Customs Water Police Station, while patrolling by boat to the Mitsubishi Company Wharf, received a report from the head of the mooring lines at the wharf stating that an empty sampan was drifting in the water near the southernmost mooring post of the wharf at the mouth of the Suzhou Creek, unclaimed. The constable went to investigate and found the sampan number to be 59. Upon inspecting the cabin, he discovered fresh bloodstains and a newly sharpened fruit knife, exceptionally shiny, with obvious traces of blood. However, the person was nowhere to be found. He immediately took the sampan to the police station to report. After investigation by detectives dispatched by the chief, it was discovered that the sampan belonged to Chen Jichang, who had disappeared the night before during the heavy rain. It was speculated that Jichang must have been murdered and his body dumped into the river. The parents, Chen Lansheng and his wife, were summoned to the police station. The two elderly individuals wept and reported the case, stating that their son had chosen an auspicious date, the eleventh day of the eleventh month of the lunar calendar this year, to get married. He was honest and did not have any romantic entanglements, but he enjoyed gambling, often losing all his earnings from a day and night of ferrying. The sampans had a rotation system for taking breaks. When Jichang was off duty, he would always go home to sleep. However, since the Mid-Autumn Festival this year, he had not been frequently at home. He left home on the twenty-third day of this lunar month and had not returned. Judging from his behavior, he certainly did not have any enemies. The cause of his murder was extremely difficult to determine. The police station took statements from the sampan operators at Chunjiang Wharf and decided to investigate the body and arrest the perpetrators.

Night Soil Contractor Lawsuit: Huang Yue'e Sues Zhang Ridong and Others for Encroachment; Hearing Postponed Pending Transfer of Case Files

The affairs of the Yangshupu Lan Road Sanitation Bureau under the Bureau of Public Works are currently managed by the Zhang Rixin, Dingxin, and Hengxin brothers from Qingpu. In Shanghai vernacular, those who engage in this trade are called "night soil contractors." Now, the Zhang brothers and their mother, Zhang Gui, have been sued by Huang Yue'e, a young woman residing on Binlang Road, and her younger brother, Huang Chengzhe, who have hired a lawyer to file a criminal self-accusation in the First Special District Court, alleging encroachment on the assets of the sanitation bureau. This case is related to an incident several months ago involving a Ma surname night soil contractor in the French Concession, who was involved in litigation in the Second Special District Court. Therefore, after receiving the Huang siblings' lawsuit, the First Special District Court requested the case files from the Second Special District Court for verification. Yesterday afternoon, Magistrate Liu Yugui opened the court. Except for Zhang Dingxin, all defendants, along with their defense lawyers, reported to the court. However, the Second Special District Court had not yet sent the case files. Magistrate Liu questioned Huang Yue'e about her age, origin, and address. He then commented, "Your brother, Chengzhe, is only eighteen years old and has not reached the age of majority. According to the law, he cannot engage in legal actions. Since his accusations are the same as yours, it would be more convenient for you to sue alone without including your brother's name." Huang Yue'e agreed. The court then inquired about the alleged facts. She stated that all the assets of the sanitation bureau that were encroached upon were located on Lan Road. She had previously sued Zhang's father. Now, part of the assets had been mortgaged by the defendants to the Fuchang Company. The amount encroached upon was no less than several hundred thousand. At this point, the plaintiff's lawyer intended to present a systematic account of the lawsuit for clarity. However, because the Second Special District Court had not yet sent the requested case files and the defendants were not all present, Magistrate Liu adjourned the hearing to a later date.

Pudong Citizens Request Establishment of a Land Bureau Certificate Exchange Office in Yangjing

Citizens of Pudong, Jia Jinfang, Huang Jiefu, Gao Gengsheng, and others, stated that the Land Bureau's certificate exchange office was moved to Kuangqiao, making it very inconvenient for the people in the Yangjing and Gaohang areas to exchange their certificates. Yesterday, they specially jointly submitted a request to the Pudong Fellow-Villagers Association to ask the bureau to establish a branch office in Yangjing Town to benefit the citizens. The original request is as follows: "The Land Bureau's certificate issuing office is located in Tangqiao Town, Pudong, which is remote. However, it is ordered that residents in the Yangjing and Gaohang areas exchange their certificates simultaneously, making it very difficult for the citizens of Yangjing and Gaohang areas. Yangjing Town is more than ten *li* away from Tangqiao Town, and Gaohang is even more than ten *li* east of Yangjing Town. Therefore, Gaohang is about twenty to thirty *li* from Tangqiao. Yangjing to Tangqiao is already far, and Gaohang to Tangqiao is even more inconvenient. It takes a whole day for a round trip. If it happens to arrive at the office when it is already full, it may take three trips to complete the process. Residents near Tangqiao arrive early because it is close by, and before the office hours begin, the workload for the whole day is already full. Those who arrive from far away have to come again tomorrow, wasting time and money. This is extremely harmful to the people and wastes their money. At this time when commerce is declining and villages are bankrupt, how can the citizens bear this loss? We have seen and heard clearly and cannot sit idly by. Therefore, we earnestly request that a certificate exchange office be established in the Yangjing Town Office (Bairen Hall), which is located in the center between the Tangqiao and Gaohang areas. The location is convenient, and Bairen Hall is also public property, so rent can be saved. Both the citizens and the finances will benefit." (The rest is omitted.)

Workers' Health Survey: "Industrial Hygiene in Shanghai" Published

Dr. Keir, formerly of the Lester Institute of Medical Research in Shanghai, has been enthusiastic about labor hygiene issues. Recently, he, along with Dr. Li Zuyou of the Institute and Ms. Zhu Yubao of the Factory Inspection Office of the Public Works Department, compiled a book based on the results of their investigation into worker hygiene, entitled "Industrial Hygiene in Shanghai." The book is in English and is published by the Chinese Medical Association. It has recently been published. The book is a report on the investigation of printing workers in Shanghai. In addition to large factories with new equipment and facilities in major bookstores, printing offices, and newspaper offices in Shanghai, most are located in *lilong* houses. The workers eat, sleep, and work in small rooms, and the hygiene is unbearable, and the lives are very pitiful. Dr. Keir and others personally visited various places for inspection, and 189 workers were questioned and examined, and they knew deeply the diseases and suffering. It is believed that those who are concerned about labor issues also want to see this book first.

Inspection Report of Zhejiang Local Bank

The 74th inspection report of the Zhejiang Local Bank's Issuance Reserve Inspection Committee states: "The members of this committee and the entrusted accountants, based on the rules of this committee, inspected the Zhejiang Local Bank's issuance reserve. The 74th inspection was held at the bank on October 19, 1935, and the results of the inspection are listed as follows: Total amount of convertible notes issued: 3,421,110.50 yuan, including silver yuan notes of 2,929,985.70 yuan and copper coin notes of 491,174.80 yuan. The total amount of convertible note reserves is 3,422,160.50 yuan, including a cash reserve of 2,469,395.50 yuan and a security reserve equivalent to 952,765 yuan. According to Article 2 of the Zhejiang Local Bank's Convertible Note Regulations, 60% of the convertible notes issued should be cash reserves and 40% should be security reserves. The results of this inspection showed that the cash reserves were over 70% and the security reserves were less than 30%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This report is hereby submitted." Dated October 19, 1935. Representatives: Zhou Xiangxian, representative of the Zhejiang Provincial Government; Wang Xirong, representative of the Zhejiang Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation; Xu Xinggong, representative of the Hangzhou Chamber of Commerce; Jin Runquan and Huang Xiaotong, representatives of the Hangzhou Banking Association; Shi Junfu and Cheng Caizhang, representatives of the Hangzhou Silver Industry Association; Wu Qiao and Zhang Facheng, representatives of the board of directors and supervisors of Zhejiang Local Bank; Accountant Han Zude.

"Jin Ping Mei" Published: Seventh Volume of Rare Books of Chinese Literature

The "Jin Ping Mei" is a top-notch work of Chinese classical novels, and the discovery of its Wanli early edition is a major achievement in Chinese literary history. The Peking Library spent 1,800 gold pieces to acquire the original book two years ago. Last autumn, in response to the requests of scholars and professors, 200 copies were printed and sold for 50 yuan each. The book is so highly regarded by scholars. Shanghai Magazine Company is now publishing rare books of Chinese literature and will include the book as the seventh volume. Since the sale of the pre-orders, dozens of letters have been received from readers from all over the world inquiring about the publication date. However, the length is large and cumbersome. The full book has 100 chapters and more than 700,000 words, so it is divided into five volumes. The first two volumes will be published today and the third volume will be published on the 9th of next month. Each volume also contains 40 illustrations selected from the collection of the former Qing Palace. The details of the strokes are better than any other version. The reproductions are printed on heavy-duty copperplate paper, which is extremely beautiful. The price of each volume is 30 cents for the popular edition, 60 cents for both volumes, 40 cents for the special edition, and 80 cents for both volumes. There is also a color spring cloth cover with gold-stamped hardcover, which is magnificent and can be published on the 15th of next month. The actual price is 2.50 yuan. Today, there is also a hardcover edition of *Slapping the Table in Amazement*, which is also made with the most beautiful color spine and gold stamping, bound into a huge volume. The actual price is 1.40 yuan, which is sure to make readers love it. It is different from the common hardcover edition. For out-of-town orders, postage is free. In addition, pre-orders for the book will end at the end of this month, with only 5 days left, and there will be no extension. If you do not order this time, you will never have the opportunity. The popular edition is 17 yuan and the special edition is 24 yuan. The average cost per book is only 30 cents.

Lawyer Wang Xuewen Practices Law

Lawyer Wang Xuewen is the daughter of Mr. Wang Yunwu, general manager of the Commercial Press. She graduated from the Soochow Law School and has a Bachelor of Laws degree. She is well-versed in the study of law and speaks English and Japanese. She has written *A History of Comparative Criminal Law* and translated *Studies in Anglo-American Law* and *Ancient Chinese Economic Thought and System*. She also co-authored a comprehensive English textbook for high school with her brother, which was popular for a time. Recently, she was granted a lawyer's license by the Ministry of Judicial Administration without examination, and was approved as a member by the Shanghai Bar Association. She is now working at the Zhonghui Law Firm on Avenue Edward VII, practicing law in collaboration with lawyer Lin Biao and others.

The middle and lower reaches of the Yangtze River are cloudy and cold, with gradual clearing. Westerly to northerly winds are slightly strong. The East China Sea is cloudy with rain and strong southeasterly to southwesterly winds. There is rain around Taiwan, with winds generally directional. Educational News

Suzhou Boy Scouts Grand Review and Camp Opening Ceremony Held Yesterday

(Zhenjiang Correspondent) The sixth Jiangsu Provincial Elementary and Middle School Boy Scout Grand Review and Camp officially began yesterday. The opening ceremony was held at the Provincial Public Stadium at 9 AM. A total of 159 Boy Scout troops, totaling 5,080 people, attended, along with more than a hundred guests and journalists. The opening ceremony began with an opening speech by Zhou Shaocheng, member and director of the organizing committee, followed by a speech by Zhao Fansheng, representative of the national headquarters. The ceremony concluded in less than an hour, followed by review preparations and curriculum competitions. At 7 PM, the elementary school group held a speech contest, and the middle school group held a bonfire party. Details are recorded below.

Attendees

Attendees included Ling Shaozu, member of the Provincial Executive Committee, Ke Boxun, representative of the Provincial Government, Zhao Fansheng, representative of the national headquarters, Zhang Qingyuan, magistrate of Zhenjiang County, Zhou Shaocheng, member and director, Shi Shunyuan and Wu Jianzhen, deputy directors, and members and judges Yuan Zongze, Zhou Qizhi, Xiang Hongjun, Yuan Ying, Yang Zeqing, Guo Jitong, Li Qifan, Chen Bangcai, Chen Kanghe, Leng Xueqiao, Jiang Zhen, Gai Qixin, Yu Bingjun, and journalists, totaling more than a hundred people.

Boy Scout Attendance

The total number of Boy Scouts from various regions included 61 middle school Boy Scout troops, totaling 2,579 people, 4 independent middle school Girl Scout troops, totaling 158 people, 12 affiliated middle school Girl Scout troops, totaling 365 people, 65 elementary school Boy Scout troops, totaling 1,556 people, 5 independent elementary school Girl Scout troops, totaling 96 people, and 12 affiliated elementary school Girl Scout troops, totaling 299 people, for a total of 5,053 Boy Scouts in attendance.

Opening Speech

At around 9 AM, the Boy Scout troops arrived at the Provincial Stadium from the campsite and the opening ceremony and 20th anniversary celebration began. Director Zhou Shaocheng gave an opening speech, with the following key points: 1. The significance of the review lies in looking at the present and preparing for the future. The review can provide the following assessments and hopes: (1) Whether the Boy Scout training is rigorous, (2) Whether the organization is sound, (3) How well prepared they are, (4) It can provide a comparison of the achievements of each troop and the opportunity for each troop to learn from each other. 2. After the review, I hope everyone will pay attention to two points: (1) Each Boy Scout should be prepared to increase their responsibility as a Boy Scout, (2) Be loyal to the party and the country and work hard for the nation.

Speech from the National Headquarters

Zhao Fansheng, representative of the national headquarters, gave a speech, stating in brief: The Boy Scouts of our country share the same fate as the nation. Only when the status of the nation increases can the youth cause progress. Our country is economically and militarily backward and cannot compete with the great powers, but we have a strength, which is the unity of our 400 million compatriots, which can save us from extinction. I hope the Jiangsu Boy Scouts will maintain the glorious history of the past 20 years, integrate the history of the Boy Scouts and the history of the nation, so that the Chinese nation can achieve the path of rejuvenation. After the speech, the Boy Scout song was sung and the ceremony was declared complete.

Competition Details

There were a total of 13 competitions today, including elementary and middle school climbing, elementary and middle school men's and women's drills, elementary school men's and women's observation, middle school army commander, middle school men's and women's first aid, and middle school women's shooting. Although the weather was clear today, there was a strong sense of rain. The review was completed at 4 PM, and then it drizzled again, and the weather turned cold. There was a hope for sunny weather. The organizing committee held a judge's meeting at 9 PM on the 24th, and everyone thought that because of the bad weather, it was unpredictable whether all the competitions could be completed. The competition results must be announced after all the competitions have been completed. If all the competitions cannot be completed due to rain, then all the results of the completed competitions will be canceled. It is deeply feared that after the partial results are announced, each troop will consider its partial results as its total score, which will inevitably lead to disputes. Therefore, the results of today's competitions cannot be announced and all the judges have kept their mouths shut.

Today's Items

(1) Elementary School Boy Scout Group, (A) Semaphore Two Flags, (B) Fire Making, (C) Semaphore Single Flag, (D) Building a Lookout Tower, (E) Knot Tying, (2) Elementary School Girl Scout Group, (A) Knot Tying, (B) Semaphore Two Flags, (D) Fire Making, (E) Semaphore Single Flag, (F) Sewing, (3) Middle School Boy Scouts, (A) English Semaphore Two Flags, (B) Knot Tying, (C) English Semaphore Single Flag, (D) Fire Making, (E) Building a Lookout Tower, (F) Night Navigation, (4) Middle School Girl Scouts, (A) English Semaphore Two Flags, (B) Knot Tying, (C) English Semaphore Single Flag, (D) Fire Making, (E) Sewing.

Ministry of Education Statement: Annual Survey of Secondary Schools, Monroe's Remarks Are Incorrect

(Nanjing, 25th) The Ministry of Education, in response to a report in the Shanghai newspaper on the 24th, stating that Dr. Monroe said at the Cultural Foundation that the Ministry of Education's survey of secondary schools only went up to the 19th year of the Republic, believes that this is not consistent with the facts and makes a solemn statement. Three Meetings of the Ministry of Education Medical Education Committee

Under the Ministry of Education Medical Education Committee, there are three committees: (1) Nursing Education Committee, (2) Midwifery Education Committee, (3) Primary and Secondary School Health Education Design Committee. The Nursing Education Committee met at the Ministry of Education on the 23rd, the Midwifery Education Committee met from the morning to 2 PM on the 24th, and the Primary and Secondary School Health Education Design Committee met in the afternoon of the 24th. Many resolutions were made, and it is reported that they will all be submitted to the Medical Education Committee on the 25th for a decision. Many motions were discussed and decided at the Nursing Education Committee and the Midwifery Education Committee. Among them, there are common points, and the more important matters are summarized below: (1) Because the nursing and midwifery schools in various provinces and cities used to be managed by the civil affairs departments or health bureaus and the health sections of the public security bureaus according to the old administrative system, it was difficult for the education departments to directly handle school administrative matters. In the future, it is planned that the education departments of various provinces and cities will be the administrative organs directly managing nursing and midwifery schools, and the health bureaus and the health sections of the public security bureaus will assist and supervise. (2) Resolved the flexible implementation methods of the standards for the establishment of nursing and midwifery schools in various provinces and cities. (3) Resolved the communication methods between nursing and midwifery schools. (4) Formulated the salary training methods for nurses and midwives. (5) Resolved (5) Resolved the passport methods. (6) Formulated bonus methods for nurses and midwifery students to encourage further studies. (7) Resolved how to change the standards for running nursing and midwifery schools in remote provinces due to economic and talent backwardness. (8) Resolved how to investigate the content of public nursing and midwifery schools. (9) Resolved other issues related to nursing and midwifery education. The Nursing Education Committee and the Midwifery Education Committee were chaired by Yan Fuqing, and the Health Education Design Committee was chaired by Gu Shusen.

Jiangsu Education Department Establishes Key Points for Inspection of Education Bureaus in Various Counties: Each Semester Must Inspect at Least 30 Schools in Rural Areas, Notice to All County Education Bureaus to Comply and Not to Treat It as a Mere Formality

The Jiangsu Education Department issued a notice to the Education Bureaus of various counties, stating that the heads of the Education Bureaus of various counties or the heads of the Third Section of the county governments that have been abolished should follow the department's instructions to go to the countryside for inspection. Each semester, they should inspect at least 30 educational institutions or more, so as to fully understand the actual situation of education in the county. This has already been notified in the past. Recently, it has been found that a small number of heads of the Education Bureaus or the heads of the Third Section of the county governments have not been able to comply with this requirement. In order to urge them to proceed, six key points for the heads of the Education Bureaus or the heads of the Education Sections of the county governments of Jiangsu Province to pay attention to when going to the countryside for inspection are specially formulated and attached with an application form for reference. In addition to issuing separate orders, the notice is hereby issued to the heads of the bureaus to strictly comply with the requirements and not to treat it as a mere formality. Attached are the key points for the heads of the Education Bureaus or the heads of the Education Sections of the county governments of Jiangsu Province to pay attention to when going to the countryside for inspection: (1) The head of the Education Bureau or the head of the Education Section of each county should inspect at least 30 rural educational institutions (primary schools and social educational institutions) each semester, and the inspection should be divided into two times, with at least 10 institutions inspected each time. (2) The head of the Education Bureau or the head of the Education Section should reward or punish or instruct to improve each institution at any time according to the merits of the handling results, and report the reward and punishment or improvement methods to the department for record. (3) The reward and punishment or improvement solutions for the head of the Education Bureau or the head of the Education Section to inspect each institution should be submitted to the department for record four times a year before the end of October, January, April, and other months. (4) When the provincial supervisor comes to the county for inspection, if the head of the Education Bureau or the head of the Education Section cannot go to the countryside for inspection in accordance with the regulations each semester, and the rewards and punishments and improvements are mostly inconsistent, and they cannot be submitted to the department on schedule, the Education Department will give them a reprimand, demerit, or salary reduction respectively. (6) The reporting form used by the head of the Education Bureau or the head of the Education Section to inspect the rewards and punishments or improvement methods in the countryside is prescribed and issued by the department for filling in. (In order to understand the head of the bureau or the head of the section's busy affairs, the text can be omitted. The name of the institution, the name of the director, the general overview of the inspection items, the reward and punishment or improvement methods, the inspection date, and the handling date are filled in on the application form used by the heads of the Education Bureaus or the heads of the Education Sections of the county governments to inspect each educational institution in the countryside. The general overview of the inspection items in the right table is specifically for the items that need attention during the inspection at that time and need to be rewarded or punished or improved. Those that are ordinary and do not need to be dealt with can be exempted from filling in the handling date, which refers to the date of implementation of the punishment and improvement methods.

Little Men (Seven) (Five)

—Original by Ms. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

Little Plum, pleased with this polite enthusiasm, treated her kindly and invited her to sit in the nursery. But Nan En insisted, "No, I want to see the boys and that warehouse!" She ran off, waving her hat with the hatband. Later, the hatband broke, and the hat flew onto the grass, carried away by the wind. She still moved forward towards her destination, without looking back.

The boys saw her coming and shouted, "Hello, Nan En!" She jumped into their ranks and proudly declared:

"I want to live here!"

"Hooray! Unbelievable!" A shout came from the wall. Looking up, it was not Tian Tian but Tao Mo. He had been perched high on the wall. He and Nan En were alike, so hearing that she would be staying for a long time, he anticipated many future "games."

"I can be a batter: let me try," Nan En said. She was good at everything and unafraid of hardship and blows.

"We've already finished playing ball, but even without your help, we beat them."

"Wait a minute, I'll beat you in a race," Nan En replied, feeling that she could boast about this.

"Can she really?" Nai De asked, puzzled.

"A girl is pretty good at running," Jie Ke replied, looking down at Nan En, expressing his approval pompously.
