Spring and Autumn

Tidbits

— (Gan Yu)

Past sins can be repented of today; future greatness can only be created today. – On life’s journey, only “today” is the most precious and most important!

Even though “the world's customs are declining,” it’s not that “people's hearts are no longer what they used to be.” If you say the ancients were all improvements, then in the times of Yao and Shun, where did the Four Evils come from?

Someone who is reserved and speaks little is not necessarily “foolish”; someone who is eloquent and speaks quickly is not necessarily “wise.”

It’s better to have no one who slanders me behind my back than to have someone who praises me to my face.

If you take things in the world seriously, then everything is hard to be satisfactory; if you can be optimistic, then everywhere is a happy place.

You must move forward with “hope,” not wait with “hope.”

Those who labor with their minds govern others does not mean that you oppress them; those who labor with their bodies are governed by others does not mean that you are their slaves.

Heaven is you, hell is also you, it just depends on what you do yourself.

Don't Forget Your Roots

— Yan

I heard that Feng Yuxiang would call his son to him every day and ask him, "What does your old man do?" His son would always answer, "My old man is a soldier." This is because Feng himself came from the military, endured all kinds of hardships, and achieved his current position. He tells his son not to only know him today but to forget him yesterday, giving him a good lesson in not forgetting his roots.

Because Feng taught his son not to forget his roots, I was reminded of the stories of three wealthy Shanghai families who took not forgetting their roots as a family motto. One family is named Li. Their late Mr. ××, who died not long ago, served as an official in the late Qing dynasty and also did a lot of beneficial public works in the locality during the Republic of China, earning everyone's love. However, he had a very difficult childhood and worked as an apprentice in a blacksmith shop, working the bellows by the furnace every day. Later, he felt that this work was unpromising, so he resolutely sought advancement, studying hard to gain admission to school and passing the imperial examinations, earning an official position. At this point, he, seeing that he was born in hardship, feared that his descendants would die in comfort, so in the family hall where the ancestral tablets were enshrined, he placed a small bellows as an offering, telling his descendants to look at this thing and not forget the origins of their ancestors in hardship, and to always be vigilant. Another family is named Chen. Their ancestors made their fortune by carrying loads on a shoulder pole to buy old goods from street to street. He feared that his descendants would forget their roots and become arrogant and dissolute, so he also placed a pair of old goods shoulder poles in the family hall as an eternal family teaching. There is also a family named Zhang, whose family hall has a pair of water buckets, also to make it known to their descendants that they should not forget that their ancestors started by carrying water while enjoying themselves. These three things in the three family halls were all very effective, because up to this day, the descendants of these three families have been able to not forget their roots and carry on the family business.

In the past, whenever someone rose from humble beginnings to great heights, they would forget the past as quickly as possible, and they would not want to leave any trace of the past in their descendants' minds. Therefore, the wealth or status in the hands of the father was rarely kept in the hands of the son. Today, there is no shortage of people who have risen from poverty, so although it is not necessary to imitate the furnishings in the family halls of the three wealthy families, the three words "don't forget your roots" should be made into a plaque and hung in the central hall to show to the descendants.

Modern Girls

— Qiu Zi

A friend came from Jinan and told me that there are modern girls in the streets of Jinan now. They dress fashionably, wearing qipaos and flesh-colored stockings. From a distance, they look like fairies. Upon closer inspection, it turns out to be just flesh color, and there are no stockings at all. It turns out that they have an open mind and hire people to paint flesh-colored stockings on their jade legs. The silk patterns are completely visible, looking like real silk stockings, almost indistinguishable from the real thing, and the luster is even better. The price is eight yuan in national currency for each painting. After the painting is finished, they must avoid washing or scrubbing, otherwise, they will wash away the glamor and return to the original state. The toes are painted with red, which is extremely bright. On top of the two big toenails, there are also painted blue sky and white sun, which is almost unparalleled in its bizarreness.

Originally, it was hot, and it was okay to go barefoot. At most, stocking merchants would complain. Now that they are barefoot, they still need to apply makeup and pretend to wear silk stockings. What is the purpose? Each painting costs eight yuan in national currency. At three times a month, it costs at least twenty-four yuan, which is more expensive or cheaper than buying silk stockings? If you say that there is plenty of money, then you can donate one yuan or half a yuan more to the disaster victims who are waiting to be fed. Saving a life is more than just building a seven-story pagoda. Why not think of this, but instead paint the blue sky and white sun on the big toes, thinking that this is the only way to achieve the ultimate in modernity? Isn’t it a strange thing?

— Juan Yin

Go find a way for the nation to survive in the flames of war.

Small Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty: Struggling to Survive, Watching the Beloved Grandson, Embracing and Crying, Remembering the Past in a Famine Year, Sowing Wheat and Inviting Disaster

Because my dad has to fight with others for water during the day, and he can't get much water anyway, my dad changed his method. He let people fetch water during the day, and when everyone was asleep in the middle of the night, he would go to work calmly. From April to June, our wheat grew very well. We estimated that we could harvest five or six hundred catties. Although the wheat planted by other families was watered later than ours, they also had some harvests. Relying on these two wells, the whole fort was always better than other places. Mrs. Zhou said: I don't understand the affairs of your Northwest, but I know about the crops in the South. The most difficult thing about crops is the period when the old grain is gone and the new grain is not yet harvested. Although the wheat you planted is growing very well, it has not yet been harvested. According to what you said, the food you eat has long been mixed with grass roots. It has been a few months now, what have you been eating? Yueying said: You are right, although we planted several hundred catties of wheat, it is only good to look at, but our stomachs are getting more and more uncomfortable every day. As for food, rich families may still have some, but poor families like us can't borrow or buy it, so we can only eat more grass roots. This can also be said to be a strength for wealth, because our wheat fields are constantly watered, and there are many weeds growing, so we brought these weeds back and cooked them with water to eat. The grass grew back on the ground after we pulled it once, so we ate boiled weeds like this for two months. (249)

Records of the Lingering Fragrance

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Speaking of the word "demon," the gardener's voice was almost inaudible.

Li Lianying immediately felt hesitant after learning the details of the matter. He pondered silently, because he already believed that what the gardener said was true. In the late autumn, a single magnolia flower blooming was indeed an ominous anomaly. However, he also knew that the Empress Dowager was a deeply superstitious person, who usually paid attention to choosing auspicious days and auspicious times, and wished she could see the words "happiness" and "longevity" everywhere, and hear auspicious words or praises all the time. If such an ominous message were conveyed to her, I really don't know how much trouble it would cause her! So it was Li Lianying's turn to play the pipa himself. However, he was, after all, an old, slick fellow with many tricks. After hesitating for a while, he already had a plan in mind.

"Since there is really such a strange thing, I will certainly report it to the Old Buddha!" He said to the gardener, "There is nothing for you to do now. Go back and take care of it carefully! When the Empress Dowager wants to ask you, I will send someone to summon you!"

This was at eight or nine o'clock in the morning! The Empress Dowager was still dressing and preparing to go to court, and I was also serving by her side. Suddenly, Li Lianying hurried in, and all of us turned our heads together, focusing our attention on his face. (445)

鴟梟

— 茸餘

In the morning, when I wake up and hear the crow cawing a few times above my head, I must spit at it and curse it a few times. In reality, crows have mouths; how can one prevent them from calling out? However, its call is just a little unpleasant, and it doesn't really cause any harm to people. Why bother cursing at it? This is the crow's misfortune! Among the birds, the owl shares a similar fate with the crow. When it emits a mournful cry in the dark of night, it similarly causes people to feel disgust and aversion.

The appearance of an owl is such that it has wide eyes and a round face, much like a cat's face. Therefore, it is commonly called a "cat-headed eagle." Moreover, it is naturally fierce, hiding during the day and coming out at night, and it enjoys eating its own kind, which adds another layer of disgust for people. When it cries, it first pauses and stutters as if saying "Carry out! Carry out!" Then, it lets out a long, melodious cry, like the sound of a bell. So, villagers also call it "bell-ringing crow." According to old superstitious legends, "Whenever it cries mournfully, there will surely be a death in the neighborhood." Therefore, whenever someone wakes up in the middle of the night during a windy, moonless night and hears its cry, it is bound to make one's hair stand on end, suspecting that some ominous event will occur. Because of this legend, I was once fooled by someone when I was a child. Someone told me, "It's crying 'Carry out! Carry out!' It must be talking about someone's death. As long as you put your ear to the mouth of the jar, you will be able to hear clearly which person has died." Driven by curiosity, I spent a sleepless night, and whenever it cried, I quickly put my ear to the mouth of the jar to explore the secret of what it was crying. The result, of course, was failure.

Its nest also likes to be made on top of tall ginkgo trees. Those tall ginkgo trees are the source of neighborhood myths: what with lightning strikes, snake spirits, and the appearance of tree gods! People will naturally add to the associations. It actually chooses to live here. How can one not regard it as an ominous and mysterious bird!

Travel Notes

Autumn in Wu Mountain

— Zhu Xi

Time flies like an arrow, and in the blink of an eye, the autumn scenery is gradually fading. With the art of playing chess, white flowers, yellow chrysanthemums, and plump crabs, the autumn scenery is already a feast for the eyes. In this season, Mandarin Duck Lake in Jiaxing is undoubtedly a famous scenic spot. The misty scenery from the top of the Rain Tower is more than enough to make people linger. Suzhou, in this autumn season, of course, also has many famous scenic spots for sightseeing. They are written below to serve as an experienced guide.

Red Leaves of Tianping: At the foot of Tianping Mountain is the ancestral tomb of Mr. Fan Zhongyan. There, the mountain rocks are arranged side by side, like ten thousand scepters paying homage to the heavens. As a scenic spot for the virtuous, it embellishes the mountain with majestic scenery.

The foot of Tianping Mountain is covered with maple trees. In this time of gradually fading autumn light, the maple leaves gradually turn bright red, a sheet of red light, like clouds rising and mist gathering, as if there were peach and apricot trees everywhere. It truly contains boundless poetic and artistic charm! Tianping Mountain is located on the west side of Suzhou City. It is about five or six miles past Mudu by the Fan Road. Recently, the Suzhou-Mudu Highway has opened for cars, making round trips very convenient.

Osmanthus Flowers of Dengwei: Dengwei Mountain in Guangfu Town is famous for its plum blossoms. When spring arrives in the world, the foot of Guangfu Mountain is covered with plum blossoms, opening like a sea of fragrant snow. However, the prosperity of the osmanthus flowers in autumn is no less than that of the plum blossoms in spring. When the osmanthus flowers are in bloom, the rich fragrance of osmanthus has already wafted into the cabin when the boats dock at the pier. The osmanthus flowers in Guangfu, starting from the top of Tiger Hill, Jianxi Kiln, and villages everywhere, are truly blooming like gold all over the ground, extremely resplendent. The Suzhou candy stores and cake shops send people to purchase these osmanthus flowers, which produce several thousand yuan a year and are a byproduct of local agricultural products. Guangfu is located relatively far away, but the Suzhou-Fu Highway is being built at an accelerated pace. In the near future, after the highway is completed, transportation will be much more convenient for travel.

Water Chestnuts of Nantang: Suzhou is a land of water. The clear waves in Huangtiandang outside Fengmen City, with the fragrance of lotus spreading for ten miles, is not only a scenic spot in summer. Even in autumn, the green water chestnuts have already grown and matured. Eating them raw is tender, fresh, and delicious, and they are very fragrant and glutinous when cooked. The water chestnut leaves float green on the water, like jasper. When the breeze rises, the water chestnut waves sway with the wind, creating ripples. Embellished with the rural children picking water chestnuts, the wonderful scenery is truly like stepping into a painting.

Reed Flowers of Stone Lake: Reed flowers are everywhere in Stone Lake at the foot of Shangfang Mountain. As the autumn light fades, the reed stalks release pure white flowers, a sheet of silver light, embellishing the lush green reeds, majestic and unrestrained, truly a unique scenery. The reeds in the lake are worth about a thousand yuan each year. In addition to being used as firewood, they can also be used as skeletons for funerary items and for making brooms and other various items.

Autumn Scenery of Dongting: In the clear and crisp autumn air, the vast lake waves are as still and blue as a mirror. The vastness and charm of Taihu Lake are truly no less than those of West Lake. The East and West Dongting Mountains stand facing each other in the lake. The East Dongting Mountain has a circumference of more than fifty miles. Climbing to the top of Moli Peak, the entire lake view can be seen, and the seventy-two peaks can be counted one by one, embellished with a few returning sails. This kind of scenery is full of poetic and artistic charm, making people reluctant to leave. The West Dongting Mountain is surrounded by peaks, very majestic. The Piaomiao Peak stands high above the entire mountain. The Biluo Peak, which produces the famous Biluochun tea, is located on the side of the Piaomiao Peak. In addition to the East Mountain producing loquats and the West Mountain producing bayberries, the pomegranates in autumn are as big as bowls, with red seeds like rubies, and the taste is also very sweet. The scenery of Dongting is very beautiful, but unfortunately, transportation is not very convenient, which is a slight drawback.

The Third Round of Long-Term Loans Concludes - Most Expired Loans Are Rolled Over -

Yesterday, the 25th, was the third major period for the conclusion of long-term loans in the financial industry. Due to market conditions, various parties ultimately lacked the ability to repay, so most of the loans were rolled over. However, for the sake of their own interests, the creditors were unable to provide as much as they wanted. It is estimated that no less than one-third of the money shops and even a small number of banks faced tightening, trying to recover their funds but struggling to succeed. Therefore, the result yesterday was that the total amount of loans expiring at banks reached 7.34 million, of which only 600,000-700,000 was in deposits, while more than 6 million was in outstanding loans. Naturally, all the indebted clients rolled over their loans, with only a small amount of tens of thousands being recovered. The total amount of loans expiring at money shops even exceeded 15 million. The Chamber of Commerce had announced a flexible solution, so the results of the negotiations were free of difficulties. The hardship was that the money shops were unable to recover their own receipts and disbursements, which posed a major problem. According to a reporter's investigation yesterday, an important figure said that nine out of ten of the long-term loans expiring this round were rolled over, so there was no problem. However, due to the large gap between receipts and disbursements, there was a disparity between joy and hardship. The previous two periods (the 15th and 20th) were barely survived. Now (the 25th) and the end of the month have more than 30 million expiring, which is likely to cause some movement. It is not expected to have a major impact. Most of the Ningbo banks' long-term loans have been consolidated and settled. Although there are 2-3 million expiring at the end of the month, arrangements have been made to roll them over uniformly. Interest rates were divided into six market prices, ranging from 8.75 yuan to 10.05 yuan. In addition, it is heard that Chinese banks have many bad debts in their long-term loans. Even if the debts are active, it is feared that most of them will only be rolled over in this difficult key.

The yarn market rose in the afternoon after falling in the morning, resembling a violent storm. With the surge of capital, people were enthusiastic, speculators were active, the market was unusually flush with chips, and the market was extremely chaotic. There were many rumors. Ultimately, with the margin hovering at a high level, more buyers emerged, and market prices continued to rise. The outlook remains turbulent. It is reported that 1,000 bales of Double Deer 20s yarn and 50 bales of Red Crest Star will be delivered in October.

This Month's Marked Yarn Reaches a High Price Before Departure

In the morning session of the marked yarn market, the near month was still high, and the margin rate also opened high. Sentiment was still good, but a slight softening appeared in the mid-session as the market had risen sharply for several days, and short covering took advantage of the opportunity to exit. However, the marked cotton head opened with the far month suddenly falling by four jiao and a half. In the second round, selling intensified, and the market was slightly flush with chips. All months declined by more than one yuan, but large firms such as Changfeng and Dafeng continued to pull in and add to their positions. At the close, there was a slight rebound. As a result, all months fell by five, six, eight, nine jiao to one yuan and one jiao compared to the previous day's closing price. When the afternoon session opened, this month was the last day of trading, breaking through 80 yuan and reaching a high of 81 yuan. Due to a lack of chips for delivery and news that margin prices were rising again, market sentiment suddenly tightened, and the far month was driven by the market to repeatedly advance. The market was particularly chaotic. The third round of this month reached 182 yuan and five jiao, and then fell back by one yuan and a half at the close to 181 yuan, an increase of six yuan and six jiao compared to the previous month's closing price of 174 yuan and four jiao. As a result, all months rose by one yuan and six jiao to two yuan and one jiao compared to the morning closing price. Grain: Most Marked Flour Transactions Concluded

Yesterday morning, the flour market opened with all months remaining stable as gold prices revisited new records, jumping horizontally to over 90 yuan in the morning session. Market sentiment was quite shaken. All months were about one point higher than the previous day's closing price. However, amidst this chaotic and uncertain situation, the excitement of industry participants was relatively reduced. Because actual transactions were not smooth and the international situation was unpredictable, the number of new buyers was scarce, and most transactions were liquidations of old positions. Although turnover reached over 5,000 bags, the market atmosphere tended to be stable. When the afternoon session opened, there were fewer transactions, and the market turned sideways. Unless there are unexpected disturbances, it may return to a flat level.

This Month's Wheat Sellers Roll Over Positions

Yesterday's wheat futures market saw prices for all months relatively stable in the morning session due to a slight improvement in foreign wheat and a continued rise in gold prices. Near-term months were up by one or two points, while far-term months were flat. However, trading was not smooth, and there was no sign of an upsurge. By the time the afternoon session opened, the current month was approaching delivery, and short positions were rolling over, so the market remained stable. In the far-term months, the market was sluggish as industry participants liquidated large quantities. Recently, the asking price for current foreign wheat has reached 6 yuan and 45 jiao, which seems difficult to trade, but exchange rate changes are unpredictable, so people are unwilling to raise prices excessively. There were no transactions in current wheat because inventory was not abundant. Customers wanted to raise prices, but factories thought the price was too high, so it became a stalemate.

Miscellaneous: Galangal Prices Soar

Galangal is produced in Guangdong Province and is a spice. Recently, there has been a shortage of arrivals, and inventory in Shanghai is also very scarce. Therefore, asking prices have risen repeatedly. It was heard yesterday that a batch was quoted at 20 yuan. It is said that the lowest price was only about 8 yuan, so the difference is as much as one and a half times.

Publishing World

Which Road Should the Publishing Industry Take?

— Yu Hui

In Mr. Leng Feng's "The Awareness the Publishing Industry Should Have" in the 27th issue of this magazine, two very obvious trends in the current publishing industry were pointed out: one is that everyone is working hard to reprint ancient books, and the other is that everyone is competing to publish sensual and erotic pictorials. Generally speaking, Mr. Leng Feng is not wrong. Bookstores with slightly more financial resources and slightly larger scale are now mostly working on the reprinting and整理 of ancient books. Smaller bookstores with weak financial resources are competing to publish pictorials and some magazines with empty content and merely beautiful forms to attract customers. This phenomenon makes people with insight feel pessimistic about the future of Chinese culture. However, I don't think this pessimism is necessary, because this is an inevitable trend. Why? From this deformed phenomenon in the current publishing industry, can't we clearly see the weak purchasing power of the general readers? What kind of customers buy series of books or series of publications with thousands of copies, or as few as dozens or even a dozen copies, goes without saying. And what kind of readers buy pictorials and publications with shallow content, I think most readers can imagine. The best customers of the current publishing industry are people like them, and although bookstores say it nicely that they are promoting culture, we can't ask them to do loss-making business, or ask them to publish books that can't find customers, or only suit the interests and needs of people who generally can't afford to buy books and magazines. Therefore, the two paths shown by the publishing industry at present are inevitable. People who care about the future of Chinese culture, I think, should not be pessimistic about this phenomenon. On the contrary, we should think of some more effective ways for the publishing industry so that bookstores do not hinder their business, and readers can get some practical benefits. It is of no benefit to be pessimistic or to curse the mistakes of the publishing authorities.

Now that we have seen the weakness of general purchasing power, we cannot deny the increase in the general readers' desire for knowledge. If they have a little spare money, they will never waste it except for some books that are indeed urgently needed for them, let alone buy something for entertainment, because they have no leisure at all. Therefore, if we can publish some more practical books and magazines, in other words, books and magazines that are more suitable for the needs of general readers, we are sure that there will be considerable sales, as long as the price is not very expensive.

Now is an era when the vast majority of people are experiencing economic panic. One out of thousands can afford a book of ten, dozens, or even hundreds of yuan, but this does not mean that the general readers do not need to read books. Therefore, in addition to letting those large-scale companies publish large books, small-scale bookstores should try their best to publish some small things. We cannot despise them because of their small size, as long as they are well-made, then what does it matter if they are small? Moreover, today there are few people who can have time to read books, and even fewer people who can have enough time to read books. Most of them spare a little time after work or after class. Therefore, it is most suitable for us to publish small magazines and books that are easy to buy and easy to read.

As for running a magazine, many people curse the proliferation of Chinese magazines today, but I don't think so. Not many of the magazines we have now are good, and the rest are all waste materials. They are just black words printed on white paper. The emptiness of the content, the lack of pure purpose, the loss of focus in selection, the shallowness of the works, and following the crowd make people feel bored. May I ask how many magazines can exceed 2,000 copies? Are they just occupying a gap in the book market in vain, letting the purchasers sneer at them? Then, if we run another meaningful magazine, can we still think it is too much? And magazines are comprehensive and fresh, easy for the publisher to run (which means easier than those large books, but it is still very difficult to run them well), and convenient for the readers to choose, easy to read, and can immediately seize newly happened things to elaborate and explain, which is what single books cannot do. Then, further, what kind of magazine do we want? We still have some magazines about domestic and foreign politics, economy, and diplomacy. We should pay attention to scientific aspects, such as social science, physics and chemistry, etc. But the main condition is that the articles should take into account the readers' level, so as not to make people have a headache after reading them. They should be written in a fluent and clear style, that is, the so-called popular science articles today. The author is only doing a kind of enlightenment work, leading the readers to a correct path, and then letting them discover and explore their own future land.

There are a few more opinions written below:

Our publishing industry now—especially the news industry—has shifted its focus from a small number of people to the majority. This is a gratifying thing. I think we may as well try to run a new type of newspaper, but although it is slightly the same as the newspaper in nature, it also combines the advantages of magazines, that is, after recording the facts, it explains them in a more selective way. I think reading the newspaper is a major event every day, and the newspaper is the most difficult thing to read. People with a lot of cultivation can understand everything, but people without cultivation can't grasp anything after reading it, which is equivalent to not reading it. From the standpoint of culture, this kind of publication gives readers a little knowledge every day, and it can be quite impressive after accumulating for a year. People's knowledge is purely gained in imperceptible, daily accumulation, and I believe it will definitely have a large sales volume. Because readers can range from college students (because their knowledge is mostly empty) to shop assistants and rickshaw pullers.

The second is to obtain specialized effects with the nature of magazines. For example, we focus on Japanese research and publish a volume every ten days or every half month to introduce Japan's national conditions or the trends of Japan's national power. The main thing is to purely focus on Japan (for example, discussions on Sino-Japanese relations and Soviet-Japanese relations can also be included) so that readers can obtain some specialized knowledge with the ability, time, and energy to read magazines.

Also, we can meet the needs of readers in various units and run various types of publications. For example, focusing on college and middle school students, the most important thing at present is things like tools, such as foreign languages. The pricing of "Japanese Language and Japanese" in Beiping is very high, but sales are very good every issue, and the sales scope is only limited to North China. It can be seen from this that the demand for such tool publications among readers is high and the vision of the publishers is correct. In addition, French, German, Russian, etc. can be organized. Our culture is backward, and we need to learn from foreign countries. Foreign languages ​​are extremely needed for us now. Taking English as an example, the English Weekly published by Commercial Press and China Press, although very boring, also has more than 10,000 readers. If our publishers are willing to make money and also do a career that contributes a little to Chinese culture, this is a meaningful way to make money. In addition, it is also necessary to organize various magazines targeting children, targeting women, etc.

In summary, my opinion is entirely for small-scale publishing agencies, and it is also a summary of the following meaning; our cultural gains from the May Fourth Movement to the present are still very poor. Are there not many college students who do not know Abyssinia and think that Harbin is a place in Russia? We need to do another enlightenment work. The object of this enlightenment work should not be limited to the intellectual class and the upper class, but should be popularized to the entire people. Therefore, I advocate running magazines, running new types of news publications, and running publications that harvest specialized effects.

Our publishing industry has always been one-sided. Seeing that A makes profits by publishing humorous publications, B also publishes collections of humorous works, and C also publishes selections of humorous masterpieces. Seeing that others publish textbooks, they also scramble to publish textbooks. But the only one who benefits is the first one who started it. The rest either lose money or sell it at a discount, as waste paper. Why don't shrewd publishers go to discover and develop their own new continent?

There is also the issue of pricing. I think it should be low. Whether a magazine is successful or not does not depend on the pricing, but on the number of readers it gains. A copy of (Sarurr'ay Evering Post) in New York only costs five cents, which is not even half the cost of the paper, but Hearst (S Harst) earns tens of millions of dollars a year because of it. The reason is that it has a large number of readers, and on the other hand, it receives a lot of advertising revenue. And the amount of advertising depends on the number of readers. Publishers are initially afraid of losing money, so they try to raise the price as much as possible. Little do they know that raising the price is a kind of suicide for publishers.

My meaning stops here. Judging from the current magazine-ization of the news industry and the news-ization of magazines, these speculations of mine may not be wrong.

Discussion of Book and Newspaper Introductions

— Leng Feng

Most publications have a column called "Book and Newspaper Introductions," which evaluates publications from the publishing industry one by one, allowing readers to use these evaluations as a reference when purchasing books. This is an excellent thing. Because the number of publications from the publishing industry is increasing rapidly, with Commercial Press releasing two or three new books daily, and other bookstores releasing three or four, or even a dozen, each month. The number of new publications in a month can truly fill houses to the point where even oxen sweat to carry them. Among these numerous publications, there will naturally be both good and bad. If no one sets standards and evaluates each one, readers will inevitably buy many inferior books, wasting valuable money and precious time, which is simply not worth it. Therefore, although "Book and Newspaper Introductions" holds a subordinate position in each publication, its importance is self-evident.

The author of book and newspaper introductions bears a great mission. Standing as a critic, they guide writers on the path they should take; they hold the key to profitability and losses in the publishing industry, acting as the driver of the cultural train, indicating the direction the publishing industry should take. Therefore, writing book and newspaper introductions is not a task that anyone can handle. Because they must understand the state of society, the trends of the times, and the detailed content of the publications. Moreover, they must use an impartial, sincere, and objective attitude to provide earnest introductions, so that readers can understand the exact good and bad qualities of a book after reading their words; so that writers can understand the shortcomings of their own works and make improvements after reading their words; and so that the publishing industry can understand whether they are contributing to culture after reading their words. If an author of book and newspaper introductions can fully achieve this level in their writing, then it can be said that their words are truly pearls of wisdom. However, how do current authors of book and newspaper introductions measure up? Aren't they far from this expectation?

Currently, authors of book and newspaper introductions are either relatives or friends of the writers, or they have financial relationships with the publishing industry. Therefore, the introductory texts they write mostly consist of slippery, perfunctory words, which have no real impact on the publications. Before writing an introduction, they don't even expend the energy to carefully read the publication from beginning to end. At most, they look at the table of contents, the preface, and get a general overview of the publication's beginning and end. Because they are not sincerely writing introductions, they don't see the need to carefully examine the publications; and because they don't carefully examine the publications, the words they write are neither incisive nor perfunctory. Such introductory texts are as good as useless, merely soiling a few pieces of white paper, and are fundamentally without benefit to the cultural world. Therefore, the general run of book and newspaper introduction articles are such that no one even glances at them. Although there may be one or two valuable articles among them, they are not noticed by the general public because gold dust is mixed in with the sand.

It seems that very few publications are completely without flaws, just like even the most beautiful woman may have a scar or a mole on her face. Now, when we flip through book and newspaper introduction articles, nine out of ten praise the publication as excellent. It is clearly written "with a faithful pen," and even when the author's writing is very difficult to understand, the introductory text always says that it is "fluent and easy to read." Such authors of book and newspaper introductions are no different from old-fashioned matchmakers who introduce marriages, using their silver tongues and flowery words to describe a dark-skinned woman with pockmarks as a celestial being, dazzling the eyes. People believe their introductions and are fooled once or twice, but they will never be fooled again. Therefore, in the current sluggish state of the book industry, no matter how excellent you praise a book in the book and newspaper introduction, it will not arouse the reader's enthusiasm for purchasing because they have lost faith in the introductory texts. Many publishing merchants understand this, so when a new book is published, the advertising text only states the general content of the book, without excessively praising it. Yes, from now on, it is wrong for book and newspaper introduction texts to simply flatter a publication. It must be reformed. Don't write introductory texts with the aim of broadening the sales channels for authors and publishers; instead, write introductory texts with the aim of preventing readers from being deceived when purchasing books. In other words, the author of introductory texts should stand on the reader's side, not on the side of the author and publisher. I sincerely hope that the gentlemen who write book and newspaper introduction texts can realize this point. This is not only fortunate for the readers, but also for the entire future of culture!

### Reading "An Overview of Yuan Dynasty Drama"

— Shen Shengshi

Published by Commercial Press, written by He Changqun, price 40 cents

This is a thin treatise on the study of Yuan Dynasty drama. After reading it, I felt that in the first four chapters, the author explored the origins of Yuan Dynasty drama from a historical perspective, seemingly with great effort. These are rarely seen in other books on the study of Yuan Dynasty drama. The author also said in their own preface: "... However, the author is confident that this book explores the origins of Song and Yuan Dynasty opera from foreign music and dance. Although it is not very satisfactory in this aspect, it is still something that Mr. Wang Guowei and most current researchers of Song and Yuan Dynasty opera have not mentioned..."

However, I think that exploring and narrating from a historical perspective, and placing it in "An Overview of Yuan Dynasty Drama," seems a little inappropriate. In a "Literary Overview," one cannot talk about literary history. In a "Novel Principles" or "Poetry Principles," one should not mix in the historical part, but this kind of mixing is common.

Since this "An Overview of Yuan Dynasty Drama" includes historical exploration and narration, and also includes "Techniques" and "Writers," if the title of the book were "Research on Yuan Dynasty Drama" and a little more material could be added, readers might find it more satisfactory.

Whether the seventh chapter of this book, "Yuan Dynasty Drama Writers," should be included in "An Overview" is not mentioned further; although it is an overview, it seems that the narration of scattered songs is too brief, so brief that one can hardly find anything about them. When it comes to short lyrics, there is only the sentence "Among the Yuan Dynasty people who were good at this, Zhang Xiaoshan was the most famous," and Zhang Kejiu's alias is also written. If one is not familiar with Xiaoshan as Zhang Kejiu's alias, it seems a little inconvenient to read.

On page 132, in the section on Guan Hanqing, it says that Guan has 13 extant plays. It should be 14, still missing Jun Dayin's Judicious Examination of the Scarlet Robe Dream.

On page 141, in the section on Bai Pu, it says that Bai Pu wrote 16 varieties of plays, but only 2 remain. Most other literary histories say 15. It may be that the play Jin Fengqin is also listed among varieties of plays because this Jin Fengqin is listed in Yuan Sun Jichang's Collection of Poetic Names of Varieties of Plays and Ming Shen Boying's Collection of Poetic Names of Varieties of Plays. Recently, Zhao Jingshen had a textual research article on Bai Pu's Jin Fengchai, researching that it is not a variety of play (the article was published in Ziyoutan). Perhaps it is not Jin Fengchai but another variety of play because I have not seen it, so I dare not speak nonsense casually.

In addition, Shang Zhongxian is now known to have written 11 types of plays, but this book only mentions 10; Qin Jianfu is now known to have written 5 types of plays, but this book only mentions 4 varieties of plays, of which 2 extant types. Also, Qiao Ji (also known as Qiao Jifu) has 11 types of plays, of which 3 are extant, but this book says he wrote 8 types of plays. Other items have not been checked one by one, but it seems that there are still omissions.

Modern Medical Publications

### Five Points of First Aid Knowledge

— Editor

(5) Intoxication (i.e., alcohol poisoning)

Those who are habitually fond of drinking will inevitably suffer from chronic intoxication in the future. This is beyond the scope of this article. Acute intoxication has approximately two pathways. One is due to excessive drinking without restraint, leading to severe drunkenness. The other is due to suicidal intentions out of shortsightedness. Those with a naturally low alcohol tolerance will become intoxicated once they drink too much. The symptoms include a pale face and red skin, nausea and vomiting, excessive talking and quarreling, and falling into a stupor. In severe cases, it can lead to immediate sudden death due to paralysis of the brain nerves and cessation of blood circulation and breathing. Mild cases will wake up on their own after half a day or a day, but they often leave behind hangover symptoms such as fatigue and headache.

Those with mild intoxication can apply a cold compress to their head to promote rapid awakening. Severe cases should be treated with utmost seriousness. It is advisable to seek medical attention immediately or send them to a hospital. In an emergency, stomach pumping and enemas can be performed, and warm, strong tea can be given to mitigate the situation while awaiting medical treatment.

(Clinic) Room 5, 2nd Floor, China Trust Company Building, Intersection of Sichuan Road and Beijing Road

(1) Yellowish Complexion, Emaciated Body, and Fatigue

He bought and took certain tonic pills, but it was like a stone sinking into the sea. Last year, he came to Shanghai and entrusted a certain doctor to inject several doses of Saibao Ming, but the effect was minimal. Later, he was introduced by the Shenbao Medical Journal and came to me for treatment. I observed that Mr. Jiang had blood deficiency and emaciation, malnutrition, and endocrine deficiency. (2) Treatment of Nocturnal Emissions and Wet Dreams

Patient Qu Kanghou, 21 years old, from Zhenhai, money exchange industry. When he was 14 years old in school, he was induced by bad classmates to pretend to be husband and wife with a certain female classmate. Over time, they gradually became intimate. The girl was three years older than Qu. After two years, the girl married, but they still secretly met. Later, he learned that the girl was a prostitute, but he had already lost his virginity to her, and it was too late. At 18 years old, he came to Shanghai. What he saw and heard inevitably moved him. He could not help but recall the past with the girl, which manifested in his dreams. He suffered from wet dreams. Later, in a daze, he had emissions even without dreams. He had taken kidney-tonifying pills, but unexpectedly they were stimulants, which worsened his condition. Last winter, he came to me for treatment. I observed that Mr. Qu had local deformities caused by masturbation. His seminal vesicle had loosened, and he was also suffering from adolescent gland deficiency. Therefore, I instructed him to take both Rejuvenation Extract and Hemei's Essence Consolidating Pills. After more than two months, his nocturnal emissions were eradicated. His adolescent gland deficiency was also well-treated.

(Note) Dr. Yu's consultation hours are from 10:00 AM to 6:00 PM, closed on Sundays.

All the children of Guangdong and the talented people from all directions can receive a good education. This is what our colleagues are deeply fortunate about. It is not only the fortune of the children of Guangdong, but also the welfare of the future of education.

The Process of Constructing the New School Building of This School

Respectfully narrated by Principal Lu Songqian

In this era of national tribulation and societal decline, the first phase of our school's new building project has actually been completed. The reason why the first phase of the project could be completed is directly due to the support of the enthusiastic elders and fellow villagers who care about education, and indirectly due to the encouragement and inspiration from all sectors of society. Therefore, we were able to achieve the expected goals in an environment full of difficulties. This is something that the colleagues of this school and the children of our fellow villagers from Guangdong who are living in Shanghai will never forget. Now that the initial phase of the project is completed and the new school building is holding its opening ceremony, it is truly impossible not to record the past events that were full of hardships. For the convenience of explanation, I will divide the process into five periods, from 1930 to August 1935, and respectfully describe them as follows:

(1) The Incubation Period – January to December 1930

In recent years, the number of our fellow villagers from Guangdong living in Shanghai has been increasing day by day due to the progress of politics, economy, commerce, and industry in this city, reaching about 200,000 or more. According to the ratio of the total population to school-age children, calculated at 15%, there should be more than 30,000 people. These more than 30,000 children who should be educated mostly choose schools established by fellow villagers as the standard for their school selection due to age, language, habits, and convenience of cultivation. Therefore, in recent years, the schools established by our fellow villagers from Guangdong in Shanghai have been developing day by day. The original school building of our school can only accommodate 600 people, but we have had to accommodate more than 1,000 people. Although it is already very crowded, there are still many people who want to enter the school. At that time, our school already had an 18-year history, and the elders and fellow villagers had high expectations for our school, and frequently hoped that we would expand the number of students and add a senior high school. According to records at that time, a total of 120 people expressed this opinion in writing (the original letter can be found in the 6th issue of the Kapok, a publication previously published by our school), and countless people expressed it orally. The colleagues of our school, in order to live up to the expectations of the elders and fellow villagers, planned to raise funds to build a new site. As soon as the proposal was finalized, even before it was announced to the outside world, Mr. Yan Lin, an elder fellow villager who was enthusiastic about education, heard about it and immediately donated one thousand yuan, saying, "A little help for the construction of the new school." His enthusiasm for righteousness and courage made the colleagues of our school very excited. Therefore, we sought opinions from all sides and prepared to take active action, and compiled and printed a special publication on the expansion plan, explaining the purpose of building a new school building; and also listed the deeds of our predecessors Yang Sisheng, Cheng Zhong, Feng Pingshan, Chen Jiageng and others who donated funds to establish schools, in order to inform those who care about education in the world. Since the release of our school's expansion plan, all fellow villagers have expressed their support, and Mr. Wen Qinfu and others from the board of directors of the Guangzhao Public Association, Mr. Lin Yibo and others, parents of students, have given strong guidance and encouragement to its implementation.

(2) The Budding Period – January to December 1931

After the release of the expansion plan, our school held an art achievement exhibition in January 1931, inviting fellow villagers and people from all walks of life to visit. We wanted to present the work achievements of our school's students to the advanced people who usually care about the situation of our school, hoping to get their criticism and guidance, and to help the implementation of our school's expansion plan. At that time, Mr. Tang Shaochuan, Mr. Chen Bingqian, Mr. Wen Qinfu and other directors of the Guangzhao Public Association, and Mr. Xu Shisong and others visited the school, and all expressed satisfaction. Mr. Chen Bingqian especially strongly supported our school's expansion plan and generously took charge of it. He immediately asked Songqian to go to the Shuidaidian Road area of Jiangwan to select a new school site; he often visited the school to discuss the site issue, and gave many instructions with his great vision and insights. The colleagues of our school were further encouraged by Mr. Chen's encouragement. During this period, Songqian, the architect Li Jinpei, and various teachers and staff members repeatedly inspected the site of the new school building, and visited many new buildings of Chinese and foreign schools in the city for reference. In the spring of that year, Mr. Chen Bingqian began to purchase a new school site for our school, working hard day and night, and with the assistance of Mr. Yang Runzhi, Mr. Cui Pinxi and others, the progress was very rapid. However, the school site must be contiguous land, and it is not easy to purchase it suddenly, because the landowners are different, some are unwilling to sell, some deliberately hoard it for speculation, the situation is complicated, and it is difficult to handle. It is known that it will not be successful without relying on the power of the government. Therefore, in August of this year, we submitted a request to the Shanghai Municipal Government to consult the Ministry of the Interior to approve the expropriation of private land according to law. However, the procedures are cumbersome and cannot be completed in a short time. Therefore, we submitted a request to the government on the one hand, and started fundraising in stages on the other, in order to advance on both sides and see the completion as soon as possible. Mr. Tang Baoshu, a school director, was particularly enthusiastic and had previously raised 20,000 yuan from Mr. Xu Wenliang, and agreed to hand it over during the appropriate period of construction. His enthusiasm for education is truly admirable.

(3) The Stagnation Period – January to May 1932

Since the September 18th Incident in 1931, due to the serious national crisis, people's hearts were unsettled, and with the January 28th Incident, this city was the first to bear the brunt, all industries were declining, and people's lives were haggard. Our school was in this difficult situation, and the expansion plan was invisibly stalled. However, education to save the country is the key plan, and our colleagues have been working day and night, never slacking off their responsibilities for a day.

(4) The Realization Period – June 1932 to May 1934 On June 24, 1932, at the board meeting of the Guangzhao Public Association, Director Tang Baoshu proposed that the construction of the new school building of our school had a considerable foundation, and proposed that the Public Association allocate 40,000 yuan for construction costs to promote its completion. Director Wen Qinfu seconded the proposal, and it was unanimously approved. The expansion plan of our school has become increasingly realized. On July 11, Mr. Wen Qinfu and others from the Guangzhao Public Association wrote to Mayor Wu Tiecheng, requesting him to serve as the chairman of the fundraising committee for the construction of our school building. Mayor Wu Tiecheng gladly accepted and took it as his own responsibility. He also hired fellow villagers who were enthusiastic about education as members of the fundraising committee, and elected Mr. Tang Shaochuan and Mr. Sun Zhesheng as honorary chairmen. Later, Mr. Chen Bingqian and Mr. Guo Dun were publicly elected as vice chairmen of the fundraising committee to assist the chairman in presiding over the committee affairs, and they all agreed. On July 27, Chairman Wu convened the first meeting at the Guangzhao Public Association. The attendees were very enthusiastic and had a detailed discussion on the progress of the committee affairs. The fundraising committee's charter was also finalized and reported to the Education Bureau for submission to the municipal government for approval and record. For the convenience of handling affairs, the following committees were established: the Education Design Committee, chaired by Mr. Wen Qinfu; the Construction Committee, chaired by Mr. Guo Le; the Finance Committee, chaired by Mr. Chen Bingqian; and the Land Purchase Committee, chaired by Mr. Guo Shun. Mr. Li Dachao, Mr. Tang Baoshu, Mr. Feng Bingnan, Mr. Zhou Qingquan, Mr. Cui Pinxi, Mr. Lao Jingxiu, Mr. Yang Meinan, Mr. Yang Runzhi, Mr. Li Zhaohuan, Mr. Huang Huannan, Mr. Tan Rongpu, Mr. Cai Chang, and Mr. Situ Shangsang were elected as executive committee members, and Songqian was elected as the general manager. Each had their own responsibilities, and they were responsible for their own tasks. With everyone working together, it was certain that they would be successful together. The chairman and all the committee members were extremely enthusiastic and spared no effort in raising funds. Our school also compiled and printed a glimpse of the achievements of Guangzhao Middle School and distributed it to various fellow villagers to help raise funds. On October 20, Chairman Wu, accompanied by Mr. Guo Shun and Mr. Feng Bingnan, went to Mr. Zheng Bozhao to solicit donations, and Mr. Zheng generously agreed to donate 50,000 yuan. Our school benefited greatly from this large sum of money, and it was not insignificant. All fellow villagers also stepped forward and donated generously. Wing On Company and Wing On Textile Company each donated 10,000 yuan, and in January 1933, the Guangdong Provincial Government subsidized 10,000 yuan. The Fundraising Committee decided that the donation amount would be 500,000 yuan, and half of it had already been raised. The enthusiasm of the fellow villagers for education is truly admirable! At the first plenary meeting of the fundraising committee, it was resolved that in addition to the 18 acres of land donated by Mr. Chen Bingqian in the name of Chen Yancan, an additional 32 acres would be purchased, making a total of 50 acres. By the time the third plenary meeting was held, it was agreed that in order to implement production education and facilitate future expansion, it was necessary to find ways to purchase more school land. It was resolved to purchase an additional 150 acres of school land, making a total of 200 acres. Immediately, a plan and various drawings were drawn up and sent to the Land and Education Bureaus for review and submission to the Municipal Government, requesting the Ministry of the Interior to approve the expropriation according to law for construction purposes. After several detailed investigations by the Land and Education Bureaus, it was approved for submission for review and handling, and it was not until August 18, 1933, that it was fully approved by the Ministry of the Interior. It can be seen that the government is extremely cautious in handling the application of people's organizations to circle and purchase private land. After our school's application to circle and purchase private land was approved, we contacted the landowners to purchase it. Mr. Chen Bingqian was entrusted by the conference to be responsible for handling this matter, and with the assistance of Mr. Li Dachao, the progress was quite smooth. (For details on the process of circling and purchasing private land, please refer to page 21 of the special publication of the foundation laying of our school's new school building.) Mr. Chen, for the convenience of students traveling, jointly presented a request to the Municipal Government with Mr. Wen Qinfu and Mr. Guo Shun to build a road (ie, Tongli Road within the Zhabei Road Tea System) directly to the new school site of our school, diagonally opposite the swimming pool in Hongkou Park. The Municipal Government approved it, and our school was responsible for the construction cost of 6,700 yuan, and the land acquisition cost was paid by the municipal treasury. It was also approved by the Municipal Government to name the road Guangzhong Road (ie, Guangzhao Middle School Road) in memory. (For details on the process of building Guangzhong Road, please refer to page 24 of the special publication of the foundation laying of our school's new school building).

On November 20, 1933, accountant Chen Riping agreed to serve as the voluntary auditor of the Fundraising Committee and was responsible for auditing the income and expenditure. Immediately, a summary of the income and expenditure from October 1932 to March 26, 1934, was compiled and distributed to the donors and fundraisers for review, and an abstract was sent to various newspapers for advertising to show credibility.

(5) The First Phase Completion Period – June 1934 to August 1935

After the school land was purchased, construction began. In June 1934, the three architects Li Jinpei, Fan Wenzhao, and Guan Songsheng (represented by Zhu Bin) jointly drew the school building plan, and then invited bids for construction. There were a total of 20 bidders, the highest bid was 189,024 yuan, and the lowest bid was 121,450 yuan. As a result, it was contracted to Guanghua Construction Factory, with a total cost of 125,000 yuan. On July 26, the Construction Bureau issued a construction license, and construction officially started that day. Wenxue Jun was hired as the supervisor. On September 9, the foundation laying ceremony was held. More than 1,000 fellow villagers and people from all walks of life attended the ceremony. Chairman Wu personally laid the foundation stone and delivered auspicious words. He also said that our school is the largest school established by Guangdong people living in Shanghai, and the mission it bears is extremely important. It relies on the efforts and cooperation of fellow villagers. Therefore, after delivering the auspicious words, he continued with a very sincere and concise speech, which the listeners were deeply moved by. At that time, a special publication commemorating the foundation laying was compiled, detailing the process of preparing to build the school building and the plans for future progress. A list of donations was appended, bound into a book, and distributed to fellow villagers and people from all walks of life for publicity. Later, Mr. Lin Bingyan donated 60,000 yuan, and Mrs. Jian Zhaonan was persuaded by Mr. Chen Bingqian to donate 50,000 yuan. Mr. Bingyan believed that the establishment of our school was originally to cultivate the children of fellow villagers equally, but the original name Guangzhao Middle School inevitably divided the boundaries due to the name of the place. Therefore, he proposed to change the school name in order to make the name consistent with the reality. On January 10, 1935, the Fundraising Committee held its tenth plenary meeting and decided to change the school name to Guangdong East Middle School. On January 19, it was announced in the newspaper and changed to the current name. Our school was built with great difficulty and relies on the enthusiastic support of fellow villagers and people from all walks of life to establish today's scale. Its great virtues and achievements will be permanently commemorated. A large sports field in the school is named Bingyan Sports Field to commemorate Mr. Lin Bingyan. A pavilion in front of the field is built as a grandstand for guests and a place for athletes to rest. A hall and office building is named Zhaofu Hall to commemorate Mr. Jian Zhaonan. This hall was originally designated as the memorial hall for Mr. Chen Bingqian's grandfather, Xinglang, but Mr. Chen gave way to virtue and wished to move it to commemorate Mr. Jian, and our school will build a separate library to commemorate Mr. Xinglang. The entire classroom building is named Bozhao Building to commemorate Mr. Zheng Bozhao. A gymnasium is named Xu Mu Gymnasium to commemorate Mr. Xu Wenliang's grandmother. A dormitory is named Yong'an Building to commemorate Wing On Company and Wing On Textile Company. A monument is erected in a suitable location in the school. The monument is square and is divided into four sides. One side is the memorial monument for Chairman Wu, one side is the memorial monument for Mr. Chen Bingqian, one side is the memorial monument for Mr. Guo Le and Mr. Guo Shun, and one side is the memorial monument for Mr. Lin Bingyan (the inscription will be recorded separately). In addition, in various cities in China and abroad, there are people who commemorate meritorious movers with road names. The cement roads in our school are wide, clean, and shaded by trees. They are now named Shaochuan Road, Zhesheng Road, Qinfu Road, Ningshu Road, Dachao Road, Bingnan Road, Pinxi Road, Huannan Road, Weifu Road, Runzhi Road, and Zhaohuan Road to commemorate Mr. Tang Shaochuan, Mr. Sun Zhesheng, Mr. Wen Qinfu, Mr. Tang Baoshu, Mr. Li Dachao, Mr. Feng Bingnan, Mr. Cui Pinxi, Mr. Huang Huannan, Mr. Cai Chang, (Weifu) Yang Runzhi, and Mr. Li Zhaohuan. The various lecture halls are places for learning, and the students have a deep impression on them. Therefore, the various classrooms are used as memorial rooms for the various gentlemen, including Yaoting Room, Jingxiu Room, Meinan Room, Yibo Room, Yanlin Room, Qingquan Room, Hongjun Room, Rongpu Room, Shangsang Room, Yicheng Room, Shisong Room, and Riping Room to commemorate Hu Yaoting, Lao Jingxiu, Yang Meinan, Lin Yibo, Lao Yanlin, Zhou Qingquan, Yu Hongjun Tan Rongpu, Situ Shangsang, Deng Yicheng, Xu Shisong, and Chen Riping. In addition, various gentlemen who donated money will be respectfully commemorated in accordance with the regulations of our school for commemorating donors. It is a courtesy to honor virtue and repay merit in order to encourage and inspire, and it is also the will of the people. The first phase of our school's construction project was mostly completed in mid-February 1935, and the entire middle school was moved in. On the day of the start of school, Chairman Wu and the various school directors came to the school to hold a ceremony and delivered speeches. The teachers and students gathered together, which was a grand occasion for a while. By August, the first phase of the project was completely completed, and the completion ceremony was scheduled to be held on October 26. As of the end of August 1935, a total of 367,231 yuan and 55 cents had been received in donations. The titles of the gentlemen who donated money and the income and expenditure accounts are published in the commemorative album of the completion of the new school building, which is omitted here.

The History of This School

This newspaper was established in January 1913 and was founded by the current principal, Mr. Lu Songqian. At that time, only the elementary school department was set up, and ordinary houses in Qingyun Lane on North Sichuan Road were rented as school buildings, named Peide School. In August 1917, it was approved by the Shanghai County Office and the Shanghai Daoyin Office for filing. In February 1919, the middle school department and the kindergarten were added. In January 1921, due to financial constraints, the middle school department was temporarily suspended.

Starting from January 1922, it was changed to the Shanghai Guangzhao Public Association, and the school name was changed to Shanghai Guangzhao Public School. In September 1923, it moved into the self-built school building in Fudexing on the Hengbang Bridge on North Sichuan Road. In addition to the continued expansion of the elementary school department, the middle school department was also restored to run junior high school. In February 1928, it was approved by the Shanghai Special Municipal Education Bureau for filing. In August 1929, it was renamed Shanghai Special Municipal Private Guangzhao Primary and Secondary School in accordance with the order of the Municipal Education Bureau. In March 1930, it was renamed Shanghai Municipal Private Guangzhao Junior High School in accordance with the order, and the primary school department was changed to an affiliated primary school (that is, the current Guanggong First Primary School). In June 1931, it was approved by the Ministry of Education of the National Government for record. In 1932, due to the January 28th Incident, many students' families moved to West Shanghai. In order to avoid affecting the students' studies, our school rented a house at the intersection of Ximolu and Xinzha Road in the Special Zone to start school. After the incident was over, it moved back to the original school to attend classes. At the same time, due to the sharp increase in students in recent years, the primary school department was particularly crowded. Therefore, the temporary school building on Ximolu Road was added to establish the Second Affiliated Primary School (that is, the current Guanggong Second Primary School).

In July 1932, preparations were made to build a new school building for the middle school department, and a fundraising committee was organized to preside over it. In August 1933, the Ministry of the Interior of the National Government approved the purchase of 200 mu of private land on Shuidaidian Road in Zhabei as the school site. In July 1934, construction began. In December of the same year, the Municipal Education Bureau approved the addition of senior high school. In January 1935, it was decided by the Fundraising Committee of the school building construction of our school to change the name to Shanghai Guangdong East Middle School, and in February of the same year, it was submitted to the Municipal Education Bureau for submission to the Ministry of Education for approval and record, and it was renamed to the current name. In mid-February of the same year, the first phase of the new school building was completed, and the school was moved into the new school building for classes.

All the original new school buildings in Fudeli on North Sichuan Road were completely used for Guanggong First Primary School and Kindergarten.

The Future Plans of This School

Although the first phase of our school's construction plan has been completed, there are countless things that need to be done in the future, and it is difficult to describe them all. Now, I will extract the more important ones and list them below:

1. Raising the school's foundation. The school's foundation is of utmost importance. After the completion of the first phase of the construction plan of our school, we must pay attention to this. We are now starting to organize the school's fundraising committee to be responsible for the implementation. (Details of the method will be given separately.)

2. Adding vocational subjects. In order to implement production education, our school will add vocational subjects in stages, taking into account actual needs. Starting from the second semester of 1935, we will first open a business department, followed by engineering and agricultural departments, etc.

3. Adding school buildings in stages. There are no less than 20 buildings, large and small, listed on the general map of our school. The ones that have been completed are: one auditorium and office building, one church, one gymnasium, one dormitory, one dining hall, one kitchen and worker's room, one gatehouse and guard room each, one memorial pavilion and one monument each, one large sports field, two small sports fields, and eleven cement roads. The ones that are currently under construction are: one library. The ones that are about to be built are: one dormitory. In addition, there are three classrooms, two dormitories, two factories, one swimming pool, and two grandstands in the sports field. We will consider building them in stages to complete the entire plan.

4. Continuing to purchase school land. The land that our school has approved to circle and purchase totals 208 mu, 9 fen, 6 li, and 2 hao. Only 109 mu, 5 fen, 3 li, and 2 hao have been purchased so far. The remaining amount should be purchased successively to meet the needs.

5. Building a new village for teachers and staff. Our school plans to set aside a part of the school land to build a new village for teachers and staff in order to solve the problem of housing for teachers and staff. (Details of the method will be given separately.)

6. Adding Guanggong Third Primary School. The area near our school is becoming increasingly prosperous, and there are many fellow villagers from Guangdong who live here. In the future, there will probably be even more. In order to facilitate children's schooling, our school plans to add Guanggong Third Primary School near our school at an appropriate time. (Our school has two affiliated primary schools, one in North Sichuan Road, south of Hengbang Bridge, and one in Xinzha Road, north of Ximolu, with a total of about 1,000 elementary and kindergarten students.)

The plans listed above include those that need to be realized in the near future or in the immediate future, and those that will take time to be completed. We should distinguish between the urgent and the less urgent, and make practical plans. In particular, we must work together to achieve success. I hope that the people of the country and gentlemen will give us guidance.

Shenbao Radio Weekly

Improvement of Crystal Oscillator

— Jian

The advantage of using crystals to make oscillators is that the oscillation is relatively stable during oscillation, but one disadvantage is that during oscillation, there is a risk of damage to the crystal oscillator, which does not cause oscillation, and the whole process is quite difficult. The improved method to be introduced here is to remedy the above-mentioned shortcomings.

The method is to insert a crystal oscillator between the screen grid and the grid filament of the oscillation tube at the same time. As shown in the first figure, (1) is the oscillation tube, (2) is the crystal oscillator inserted between the screen grid, and (3) is the crystal oscillator inserted between the grid filament. These two oscillators must be selected with equal oscillation frequency. (4) is the screen circuit matching circuit, with a self-inductance coil (5) and an adjustable variable capacitor (6) inserted in the middle. (7) is an ammeter for measuring the current in the matching circuit (4), and (8) is an ammeter for measuring the screen current. (9) and (10) are fixed capacitors.

Now, when the variable capacitor of the screen matching circuit (4) is adjusted, a strong oscillation current is caused by the crystal oscillator. At this time, if the ammeter (7) is used to measure the current in the matching circuit (4), the current changes with the increase or decrease of the capacitance C of the capacitor (6) as shown in the second figure. In the figure, the vertical axis represents the matching current, and the horizontal axis represents the capacitance of the capacitor (6). The highest peaks IA and IIA each represent the current during matching. That is, if the capacitance of the capacitor (6) is small, the oscillator (3) oscillates according to the curve of 1; if the capacitance of the capacitor (6) is large, the oscillator (2) oscillates according to the curve of II.

Therefore, in use, if one oscillator is damaged, another oscillator can be used for oscillation, so this improved method is quite convenient for mobile communication machines and the like.

New Developments in Vacuum Tubes: PC.A6E5 "Electronic Optical Adjustment Indicator Tube"

— Common Words

Due to advancements in radio manufacturing, new radios far surpass older models in selectivity, sensitivity, and fidelity. However, a significant difficulty arises in tuning. If the tuning is not precise, sensitivity greatly diminishes and audio distortion can occur. If this difficulty cannot be overcome, even meticulously designed radios will fail to perform to their full potential due to tuning challenges.

The 6E5 "Electronic Optical Adjustment Indicator Tube (Electron ray indicator tube)," is a type of so-called "Tuning indicator," which enables the most accurate tuning.

The internal structure of the 6E5 vacuum tube is shown in the first diagram. In addition to the plate and cathode of a triode, the tube contains a special "Electron Target" and an "Electro-optical Control Electrode (ray controlelcetrode)." The electron target is coated with a luminescent material, so when connected to the positive terminal of the B battery, it absorbs electrons emitted from the cathode, causing the luminescent material to glow. The size of the glowing area is controlled by the electro-optical control electrode located between the electron target and the cathode. This electro-optical control electrode is connected to the plate of the triode section, and the grid of the triode section is connected to the automatic volume control section. Therefore, the voltage on the electro-optical control electrode is related to the automatic volume control voltage. Consequently, the area of the glowing part on the electron target is also related to the automatic volume control voltage; in other words, it changes with the signal voltage. Diagram two shows two forms of electron target luminescence. In diagram A, the tuning is incorrect, no station is received, and the glowing portion covers approximately ninety degrees. In diagram B, the tuning is quite accurate, and the angle of the glowing portion is greatly reduced. Therefore, during tuning, one need only minimize the glowing portion of the electron target.

Attached are the characteristics of the 6E5 vacuum tube:

Filament (AC or DC): 6.3 volts, 0.3 amperes

B Voltage: 250 volts

Operating Conditions:

Electron Target Voltage: 250 volts

Plate Dropping Resistor (in series): 1 million ohms

Electron Target Current: Approximately 4.5 milliamperes

Plate Current with No Grid Voltage: 0.25 milliamperes

Grid Voltage at 90-degree Luminescence: -8 volts

Grid Voltage at 0-degree Luminescence: 0 volts

Tube Height: 3 and 5/8 inches, Maximum Diameter: 1 and 9/16 inches, Glass Bulb: ST'12 type, Tube Socket: Small 6-pin.

Two Telegraph Practice Airplanes

— Hua Xin

Here's an introduction to a telegraph practice machine. With just a buzzer and a set of batteries, you can practice sending and receiving at the same time. The diagram above shows its circuit. The capacitor C, which is 0.5ufd, is used to block the direct current flowing from the battery into the earpiece. The audio frequency generated by the buzzer passes through C and into the earpiece. If the key and earpiece are inserted in parallel, multiple comrades can practice communication together in one place. You might as well give it a try.

Introducing a Special Two-Tube Shortwave Radio

— Ke Qin

Recently, many different styles of radio vacuum tubes have been introduced. If amateurs still use old-fashioned vacuum tubes to build radios, the performance will inevitably be poor. There are many styles of new vacuum tubes, and the 6D6 and 76 types are quite popular because they can make the volume louder and the reception more stable. The one I am introducing now is a two-tube shortwave radio using these two types of vacuum tubes.

The circuit diagram of this machine is attached. The 6D6 vacuum tube is used for detection, and the 76 vacuum tube is used for audio frequency amplification. The detection also uses a band-spreading device. The volume is controlled by a 50,000-ohm carbon resistor.

A small variable capacitor is added to the antenna circuit. Its capacity is 0.00005. C2 is the main parallel tuning capacitor, used to adjust various wavelengths.

The reception wavelength range of this machine is extremely wide, from 17 meters to 278 meters. It uses four plug-in coil tubes. The waveband and wire number are listed in the table below.

The parts used in this machine are listed as follows:

C1: 0.00014 Variable Capacitor

C2: 0.000035 Variable Capacitor

C3: 0.0005 Variable Capacitor

C4: 0.00025 Grid Fixed Capacitor

C5: 0.01 Fixed Capacitor, Withstand Voltage 200 Volts

C6: 1 Fixed Capacitor, Withstand Voltage 200 Volts

C7: 5 Fixed Capacitor, Withstand Voltage 200 Volts

C8: 0.00015 Fixed Capacitor

R1: 1 to 5 Megohm Grid Leak

R2: 50,000 Ohm Resistor, for Volume Control

R3: 500,000 Ohm Resistor

R4: 10,000 Ohm Resistor

R5: 100,000 Ohm Resistor

R.F.S.: High Impedance Coil, 2,000 Millihenries, S.W. Switch

Because this machine has two variable capacitors, C1 should be fixed first, and then C2 can be adjusted. First turn C2 to about 20 degrees, then turn C1 until you hear a sound. Then make fine adjustments with C2. Also, because this machine has four plug-in coils, C1 should be calibrated four times, and remember the degrees, so that the next time you use it, you can save the trouble of temporary fixing.

Waveband (meters) L1 (turns) L2 (turns)

17.4I 8.3 (No. 16 Enamel Wire) 7 turns per inch 3.8 (No. 32 Silk-covered Wire) Closely wound

93-75 17.7 (No. 20······) 12 turns per inch 5.8 (Same as above) Same as above

66·150 37·7 (No. 24······) 24 turns per inch 10.8 (Same as above) Same as above

135.270 31.7 (No. 28······) 44 turns per inch 16.8 (Same as above) Same as above

The diameter of the above four plug-in coil tubes is all 1.5 inches. The distance between L1 and L2 is 1/4 inch.
